Current State of Anti-Japanese Resistance in Jiandao, Northeast China (Jilin Correspondence) 81

Detailed Account of Past Circumstances and its Organizational Content

Integration of Independent Movements by Korean and Chinese Peoples

What is Jiandao? Is it an island, a peninsula, or something nominally an island but not actually an island? Is it in the ocean or on land? Our country has a vast territory, and it is located outside the pass, so it may not be noticed by the general public. Even Japan, which regards Manchuria as its lifeline, experienced a major uprising of Jiandao residents five years ago. A member of the Japanese House of Peers said, "The uprising of the residents of a small island can be easily resolved by dispatching a warship." Thus, even some members of the Japanese House of Peers consider Jiandao to be an "island." In fact, Jiandao is not an island. It is located in the southeastern part of Jilin Province on land, and it is hilly land bordering Korea and facing Niigata, Japan, across the sea. It is a necessary route from Korea to Northeast China.

According to our country's maps, there is no place called Jiandao. The Tumen River from Maoshan downwards has many beaches along the river. The largest area of reclaimed land is in Guangji, which is about several li long and about one li wide, totaling more than 2,000 mu of land. Originally, it was silted up with mud and sand, and it was connected to the north bank of the Tumen River. Later, it separated from the bank, causing the river to diverge, forming what seemed to be an island. (Some say that in the seventh year of Guangxu, Koreans privately dug a ditch on the north bank of the Tumen River, causing the river to diverge, which may be true.) Koreans who cultivated here initially paid a rent of 8,000 taels of silver to us each year. In the 29th year of Guangxu, the Korean official began to call the area Jiandao and claimed it as Korean territory. This is the origin of the name Jiandao. In that year, Chen Zuoyan, the magistrate of Yanji Ting, negotiated twelve provisional agreements with the Korean officials to quell the unrest among the Korean people. The eighth article stated that the ancient Jiandao, which is the Guangji Valley reclaimed land, had always been permitted for Korean people from Zhongcheng to rent and cultivate, and this would continue to be handled as before. This establishes that Jiandao should belong to our country and is part of Jilin Province, which has become an ironclad case. Chinese influence also recovered somewhat at this point. After the end of the Russo-Japanese War and Korea was annexed by Japan, in the 31st year of Guangxu, Hasegawa Yoshimichi, the commander of the Japanese army stationed in Korea, inspected North Korea and arrived at Huining. The Korean people submitted a petition requesting protection for the Jiandao settlers and also sent representatives to the Governor-General's Office to appeal. At that time, Japan also investigated the convenient topography of Jiandao, which could be developed. In the 33rd year of Guangxu, Japan sent troops to Jiandao to establish a branch office of the Governor-General's Office. This was the beginning of direct negotiations between Japan and our country. After our government heard about this, it dispatched Chen Zhaochang as the border affairs supervisor to handle defense and surveying matters. At the same time, the Ministry of Internal Affairs negotiated with the Japanese ambassador. They argued with each other for a long time without a resolution. At that time, Japan considered the area east of Guangjilue as East Jiandao and the area around Helongyu as West Jiandao, as an undetermined border between the two countries. The arguments they used were based on the reasons that the Koreans mistakenly regarded the land on the north bank of the Tumen River as their own, and there was no other definite evidence. In the end, our side held firm with accurate evidence. By the first year of Xuantong, the settlement of the Anfeng Railway Line negotiations was resolved through Japan's free action. Japanese Ambassador Ijuin took the opportunity to resolve all the pending issues between China and Japan, and the Jiandao issue was also resolved at this time.

Since the establishment of the Sino-Japanese Anfeng Railway Border Traffic Agreement in the third year of Xuantong, Jiandao has become a special area for Japan to transfer and colonize Korean people, and it has also become a residence for Japanese ronin. At the same time, it is also a haven for Korean anti-Japanese patriots.

The Koreans in Jiandao are nominally allowed to migrate freely, but in reality, they are all driven there by the Japanese. Once they arrive, they cultivate the land. Although it cannot be considered a paradise, they can still live there. However, looking back at their homeland being trampled on by Japanese imperialism, they cannot help but feel deeply moved. Since Jiandao has become a special area, before the September 18th Incident, the authority of the Northeast authorities could not reach it, and the residents of the area were extremely complex. There were illiterate Korean farmers, a small number of native Jilin residents, Japanese ronin, Korean revolutionary patriots, and bandits, good and bad mixed together. Therefore, Jiandao became a source of revolution and a den of bandits. The current Jiandao has transformed from an anti-Japanese independence movement into a "People's Revolutionary Government." The process is described in detail below.

The first phase: After the Sino-Japanese War in 1894, Korea was nominally an independent country, but the Korean people were living in dire straits under the oppressive power of Japan, similar to the current situation in Northeast China. After Japan completely annexed Korea in 1910, Korean patriots never forgot their desire to restore their homeland. Therefore, they crossed the Tumen River and went to Jiandao in groups to live their lives as exiles and carry out their revolutionary movements. This was the starting point of the Korean people's revolution.

The second phase: In 1919, an independent movement suddenly broke out in Korea, and the Korean residents in Jiandao responded enthusiastically. There were more than ten independent movement organizations. In 1920, Japan sent troops to suppress them. Revolutionary patriots who had fled from Korea to Jiandao increased day by day. Therefore, they established various schools to provide education on the revolutionary movement and cultivate anti-Japanese thoughts, which took great pains. In 1921, the Korean Communist Party established a central headquarters in Seoul. These people, who had always advocated for the independent movement, transformed into communist propagandists. They also established the Dongyang Academy in Longjing, Jiandao, to promote anti-Japanese thoughts and communism.

The third phase: This was a transitional period from the independent movement to communist propaganda, leading to the establishment of the Soviet. Since 1921, communist ideology gradually became popular in Jiandao. Until 1927, it was exposed by the Japanese authorities. In addition, internal factional struggles were extremely fierce. As a result, the activities gradually subsided for three or four years.

The fourth phase: After a period of subsidence, the momentum gradually increased again. After the May 30th Jiandao Riot in 1930, it is said that a small number of communist party members from our country also joined. Therefore, the communist organization in Jiandao became more complete, and the momentum expanded day by day. The slogans were to overthrow imperialism, confiscate the property of the Jiandao Eastern Development Company, confiscate land, not pay taxes, and build the Jiandao Soviet government.

In the past, Japan adopted a laissez-faire attitude towards Jiandao. After the success of seizing Manchuria on September 18th, Japan mobilized its troops. However, after suppressing them once, the flames reignited soon after. Because most of the local people were farmers, they would return to normal and engage in farming when the [puppet] army arrived. When necessary, they would gather again and revolt. However, the Korean people's hearts are set on opposing Japan and seeking independence. Sometimes, they cannot arouse their enthusiastic sympathy for communist ideology. Therefore, the recent Jiandao Communist Party cadres have adapted to the psychology of the Korean people, stimulating the anti-Japanese sentiments of ordinary farmers, organizing peasant armies to overthrow Japanese imperialism, and uniting with the defeated righteous volunteers in Northeast China to fight against the Japanese [puppet] army. According to a survey by the Japanese authorities in 1932, four district Soviet governments have been established, implementing communist politics and leading the people in actively opposing Japanese [puppet] movements. The various organizations are described below: 1. Anti-Japanese Association: Organized by anti-Japanese Koreans and Northeast patriots. It includes landlords, capitalists, and farmers, who are united in resisting Japan, aiming to expel Japanese forces from the Northeast territory. 2. Anti-Japanese Workers' and Peasants' Guerrilla Force: Aiming to expel Japanese forces by force. 3. Anti-Japanese Self-Defense Force: Mainly to defend against Japanese forces and protect the local area. 4. Farmers' Committee: Organized as a strategy for farmers' struggles, protecting the interests of poor farmers, uniting the peasant masses, and resisting Japanese [puppet] forces, local bullies, and usurers. 5. Anti-Japanese Soldiers' Representatives Conference: Composed of daredevil teams formed by righteous volunteers, specializing in anti-Japanese atrocities. 6. Young Pioneers: Divided into organizational, propaganda, and training teams, directed by the Anti-Japanese Self-Defense Force, specializing in sentry duties. 7. People's Revolutionary Government: Originally the Anti-Japanese People's Government, later renamed the People's Revolutionary Government. It designates districts, establishes national borders, implements Soviet politics, and is the central hub of all mass organizations.

Map of the Jiandao Anti-Japanese People's Revolutionary Government Area

Legend: People's Revolutionary Government Area

Area Bordering China, Soviet Union, and Communist Party

According to a recent survey by Japan: Party members: 580 Koreans, 217 people from the Northeast (Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang); Communist Youth League members: 830 Koreans, 19 people from the Northeast; Children's Corps members: 1,950 Koreans, 14 people from the Northeast; Anti-Japanese Association members: 11,800 Koreans, 390 people from the Northeast; Guerrilla members: 565 Koreans, 16 people from the Northeast; Weapons: 440 rifles, 120 pistols, 1,800 mines. (January 3rd)

War Situation of Japanese Army Invading Longmen 82

Negotiations by Our Side Lead to Japanese Army's Retreat

Japanese Army Still Instigating Li Shouxin's Troops to Invade Westward

A dispatch from Beiping reports that since the transfer of Tang Yulin's troops from Chahar East to Zhangjiakou for training and the rebellion of Liu Guitang's troops, various Chahar provincial armies have been transferred to garrison the area. The Japanese army had an existing plan to invade Chahar Province, employing a gradual encroachment policy to seize our territory. Taking advantage of our troop transfers, they launched a sudden invasion, attempting to fulfill their grand ambitions. On the 15th of this month, Mori Ichiro, the Japanese commander of bandit suppression in Heihe, abruptly issued a preposterous notice to Zhang Renjie, our garrison commander in Chicheng. The notice was divided into four points: 1. The Great Wall line is the border between China and Manchukuo, and neither side may station troops there. Longmen in Chicheng belongs to the Great Wall line, and Chahar troops stationed there violate the agreement. 2. Troops stationed in the Chicheng-Longmen area should withdraw immediately. 3. If the troops are not withdrawn, the Japanese army will launch an attack. 4. Notices posted by the Japanese army on the Great Wall in the Longmen area have often been torn down by the Chinese side, which is an improper act. Hereafter, no Japanese notices may be torn down again, or the Japanese army will send troops to attack. A response was demanded by the 16th. This absurd notice was delivered to Zhang Renjie in Chicheng only on the morning of the 16th. While Zhang was seeking instructions, Japanese and puppet troops had already advanced towards Longmen, attacking Zhaojiaying, a position held by our troops. As for the enemy's strength, the Japanese army consisted of over 300 soldiers from a Heihe bandit suppression unit, and the puppet troops numbered over 400 from Zhang Haipeng's unit, carrying four machine guns and several small cannons. At dawn on the 16th, they advanced to the front of Zhaojiaying, a position held by our troops, and immediately fired upon the 5th Company of Hu Wenyu's regiment under Zhang Renjie's command. Our forward troops defended their positions, responding calmly while telegraphing the authorities for instructions. Contact was made between both sides in the afternoon and only stopped at night. Our side suffered slight damage, but the position remained unchanged.

After receiving a report of the battle at the front, Zhang Weifan, the chief of staff of the 29th Army in Zhangjiakou, urgently telegraphed Ping for instructions. Qin Decun then separately visited He Yingqin and Huang Fu to report everything. On the afternoon of the 16th, Huang Fu immediately sent a representative to negotiate with the Japanese military attache, Nemoto, at the Japanese embassy. Both sides agreed to first order a cessation of military action at the front and then send representatives to negotiate in Ping. Nemoto immediately telegraphed the 8th Division stationed in Chengde to convey this intention. Yesterday, the 8th Division responded, indicating agreement, stating that it was a misunderstanding, and had ordered the advancing Japanese troops to retreat immediately. Yesterday (the 17th), the Japanese army that invaded Longmen retreated towards Heihe. Our troops remain on high alert. Zhang Yunrong, the garrison commander of Zhangbei, also arrived in Chicheng from Dushikou yesterday to discuss defense of Chahar East with Zhang Renjie and Song Tielin. Song Zheyuan, the chairman of Chahar province who was visiting relatives in Tianjin, originally intended to come to Ping to discuss solutions to the Chahar East problem with the authorities, but due to an unhealed back ailment, he will not return to Ping for the time being. Everything will be handled by Qin Decun as his representative. This morning (the 18th), Qin received a telegram from Zhang Weifan reporting the situation at the front. The original telegram reads as follows: [To Director Qin Shaowen, Upon receiving a report from Deputy Division Commander Song Tielin: 1. Yesterday morning (16th), Japanese and puppet troops dispatched a small number of troops with four light machine guns to fire upon the 5th Company stationed at Zhaojiatun, carrying out harassment. Our 5th Company maintained calm and resisted steadfastly, and they retreated after about half an hour. 2. All our forward units remain in their original positions and have not moved. 3. I, the Division Commander, and Commander Zhang are both in Chicheng. Aside from already having submitted this report to the Chairman, I hereby notify you. Zhang Weifan, respectfully].

Although the Japanese army that invaded Longmen has retreated, they ordered Li Shouxin's puppet troops, who had already invaded the second and fourth districts of Guyuan, to advance westward towards the Guyuan-Binchang area. Upon receiving the Japanese army's order, the traitor Li inquired about the purpose of the advance, and the Japanese army replied that it was to inspect the situation and that they could go wherever they pleased. Li is currently hesitating. Our side now believes that the Japanese invasion of Chahar is still in progress, and is currently both negotiating with the Japanese side and maintaining strict vigilance to prevent unforeseen circumstances. (January 18th)

Circumstances of the Navy's Participation in the Recapture of Fuzhou 83

First Intercepting the 19th Route Army at Shanhai

Then Two Regiments Entering the Provincial Capital in Two Routes

A dispatch from Fuzhou reports that after the successive losses of Gutian and Shuikou by the 19th Route Army, the troops at the front mutinied one after another, and the rear was bombed by airplanes. Soldiers scattered and fled, with no will to fight. Furthermore, the Central Army and Marines surrounded Fuzhou from Gutian, Yongtai, and Lianjiang in three routes. Knowing that it was difficult to maintain their position, they issued an order for a general retreat on the 12th. Upon hearing the news, personnel from various agencies panicked and fled on the 12th, leaving all equipment to be taken away by servants and nearby residents. Unexpectedly, on the 14th, the defeated soldiers of the 19th Route Army retreated to Shanhai, where they clashed with the navy. One company was disarmed. Cai Tingkai, in his capacity as the commander of the city defense, issued a proclamation, stating that they were still deploying defenses and preparing for battle in the suburbs of the provincial capital. Merchants, fearing the devastation of the area, urgently pleaded with Sa Zhenbing to mediate, willing to provide ten merchant ships in Shanhai to transport troops across the river, while also requesting the navy to allow them to pass and not intercept them. As a result, the remnants of the 19th Route Army went through the northwest and various villages, passed through Nanhai from Shanhai, and proceeded towards Fuqing. At around 7 PM on the 15th, the vanguard of the Central Army advanced to the vicinity of Hongshan outside the West Gate, engaging in a brief skirmish with the 19th Route Army, which had not yet retreated. The 19th Route Army retreated again towards Nanhai. By about 12 AM, the 19th Route Army in the suburbs of the provincial capital had completely retreated. The two regiments of the 2nd Marine Brigade, under Yin Jiaxun and Wei Feng, immediately entered the provincial capital on land and water routes to take over the defense of the city and the Nantai area. Chen Jiliang, the commander of the 1st Fleet of the Navy, also received an order from the Navy Department to lead the Chu Tai and Jiang Yuan warships from Mawei to station in Taijiang, showing up to pacify the people. Shops and businesses immediately changed to hang the Blue Sky White Sun flag and posted slogans welcoming Minister of the Navy Chen and Vice Minister Chen. In the afternoon, Jiang Dingwen, the Commander-in-Chief of the Northern Route of the Jiangxi-Guangdong-Fujian-Hunan-Hubei Bandit Suppression Army, also arrived in the province with the 3rd Division under Li Yutang and the 9th Division under Li Yannian, stationing a part of them in the Pacification Commissioner's Office and Donghu, and the rest garrisoned outside the East, West, and North Gates. On the afternoon of the 17th, Jiang Dingwen and Chen Jiliang met at the Sanqiao Club. It is heard that Jiang intends to order the 3rd and 9th Divisions to continue pursuing the 19th Route Army in the direction of Yongtai and Fuqing. As for various Party and government agencies, they will wait for the central government to send personnel to take over. Chen Zhongjing, the special financial commissioner dispatched by the Ministry of Finance, arrived in the province on the 17th and will first take over various financial agencies and start levying taxes to avoid a standstill. (January 17th)

Bandit Liu Flees West Along the Pinghan Railway 84

Lu Army Ordered to Return to Defend

A dispatch from Jinan reports that after Liu Guitang's rebellion, he led over three thousand troops to flee to Southern Hebei, intending to return to his old nest in Southern Shandong. Han Fuju, the chairman of the provincial government and commander-in-chief of the 3rd Route Army, immediately dispatched troops to block him in Northern Shandong. Today, a long-distance telephone report from Linqing stated that on the night of the 16th, Liu Guitang's bandit troops fled near the Shahe Station on the Pinghan Railway. Due to the pursuit of the Hebei provincial cavalry brigade and Wang Qifeng's troops of the 3rd Division from behind, the bandits continued to flee west on the 17th. As of the report last night, Liu's bandits had fled west of the Pinghan Railway, heading towards Southern Henan, seemingly with no possibility of fleeing back to Shandong. From now on, the bandit suppression work will be the responsibility of Henan. Shandong has deployed anti-bandit troops in Western Shandong and Northern Shandong, including Li Yizhi's brigade of the 74th Division, Lin Binghai's 128th regiment of the 22nd Division, Zhao Renquan's militia regiment of the 2nd Route, Yun Qichang's brigade of the 81st Division, and Li Xuande's cavalry regiment. Zhao Renquan once led militia and Li Xuande's cavalry to pursue the bandits out of the province. Now that Liu's troops have fled west of the Pinghan Railway, they have been ordered by Chairman Han to stop the pursuit and return to their respective defense areas. Lin Binghai's regiment returned to Jinan, and Li Xuande's cavalry remained temporarily in Guantao and Qiuxian for vigilance. Zhao Renquan himself returned to Linqing yesterday, and his hybrid regiment also returned to defense today (the 18th). Zhan Shutang, the commander of the 81st Division, arrived in Fan County on the 16th with his directly subordinate battalions and companies, maintaining strict discipline, ensuring the peace of mind of merchants and residents. As Liu's bandits have fled far away, the alert in Fan County has been temporarily suspended to prevent their return. As for the actual strength of Liu's bandits, according to captured bandits, the bandits have over three thousand cavalry, over a thousand infantry, over two hundred camels, sixteen mortars and machine guns, and many rifles and box cannons. Along the way, they also confiscated guns from local militia and Lian Zhuang Hui, so they have plenty of guns. There are even bandits with two or several guns. (January 18th)

Suzhou

Elderly Man Crushed to Death by Express Train 85

Yesterday (21st) around 10:00 AM, the Shanghai-Nanjing express train departing from Suzhou Station struck a man estimated to be about fifty years old as it left Wai Yangqi. He was dragged under the wheels to the Yang Bridge at No. 106.

The chest was also crushed. The deceased was wearing a small cap, a black cloth cotton robe, and cloth shoes. Afterwards, the station police instructed the local Baojia Qian Genda to report the case to the court for investigation.

Wuxi

Director Wang Comes to Wuxi to Supervise Construction of New Prison 86

The case of rebuilding the new prison in our county has been designed and planned by the previous two prison officials, Han and Kong, and the estimated cost is 40,000 yuan, which has been reported to the Ministry for approval. At that time, the Minister of Justice, Luo Wengan, happened to be inspecting Wuxi and also believed that it was necessary to rebuild the new prison. At the same time, Minister Luo, based on the inspection report of Wang Yuanzeng, Director of the Prison Department, proposed to rebuild the old prison in our county into a branch prison of the new prisons in Suzhou or Zhenjiang, with a capacity of 300 inmates. After Minister Luo received the report, he specially sent Director Wang to Wuxi to supervise the project. Mr. Wang arrived in Wuxi the day before yesterday with technician Zhou Yuanfu. He first went to the prison for a detailed inspection, and then technician Zhou measured the open space behind the prison and sketched the drawings to prepare for the construction of the new prison, which took a long time. At the same time, the Wuxi Prison Improvement Association also held a meeting at the county government to discuss the prison construction funds, which were changed to 50,000 yuan. Half of the funds will be requested from the Ministry of Justice from the additional 50% surcharge, and the other half will be raised locally, so as to realize the project as soon as possible. According to Director Wang to the reporter, the drawings for this prison construction are drafted by the Ministry, and the project is the responsibility of the local government, and it will be realized in a short period of time.

Jiangyin

Jiangyin Boat from Yangzhong Meets with Danger, British Warship Passes By and Rescues 87

The Jiang boat in Yangzhong County (i.e. Taipingzhou) set sail yesterday (20th) at 8:00 AM for Taixing, when it was suddenly overturned by wind and waves in Tiejinggang. The thirteen people in the boat, including the boat owner Guo Hongren and male and female passengers, all fell into the river. At that time, the British warship Innerde (transliteration) happened to pass by, and immediately stopped and lowered a sampan to rescue the people from the river. Only the son of Zhang Minggao drowned. Those rescued include Ma Changyin, Zhu Kuizhang, Huang Hengnan, Shi Guangzhu, Chen Bingwen, boat owner Guo Hongren, Luo Wangshi (pregnant), Wang Yongxiang, Dai Chenglin, and Zhu Qingcheng, as well as two children. Each person was given two dimes. The British warship passed through Jiangyin and stopped at 3:00 PM, and the adjutant Yuan Yongrui, sent by the Captain Arnerfu (transliteration), sent the people to the Charity Ferry Bureau. Yuan Junmei, the director, ordered each person to change out of their wet clothes, had them eat a hearty meal, and then arranged for them to be sent back to their hometown by the Dayuan River steamer.

Joint Transportation Implemented Yesterday on the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway and the Zhenjiang-Yangzhou Long-Distance Bus 93

Huadong News Agency reports that in order to facilitate passengers, the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo railways have signed a joint transportation contract with the Zhenjiang-Yangzhou Long-Distance Bus Company. At the stations of Shanghai North, Suzhou, Wuxi, Changzhou, and Nanjing on the railway line, and between the Shijiaqiao and Yangzhou stations of the company, passenger, baggage, and parcel joint transportation services are mutually provided. Zhenjiang station is the connecting station. In addition to the original company's ferry facilities from Zhenjiang Wharf to Liuyi, and the company's bus from Liuyi to Yangzhou to transport passengers and baggage, the company has added buses to pick up and drop off passengers and transport baggage between the company's Zhenjiang Wharf and the railway bureau's Zhenjiang Station, in order to connect seamlessly. The joint transportation method has been implemented since yesterday. The details are as follows:

Announcement of Implementation 94

The Traffic Department of the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways Administration issued an announcement: In order to announce the matter, the five stations of Shanghai North Station, Suzhou, Wuxi, Changzhou, and Nanjing on the Shanghai-Nanjing line will, starting today (January 21), begin providing mutual ticket, baggage, and parcel joint transportation services between the Shijiaqiao and Yangzhou stations of the Zhenjiang-Yangzhou Long-Distance Bus Company. For detailed information, please inquire at the Shanghai Railway Business Office, the Nanshi Branch, or the station masters of Su, Xi, Chang, and Zhen, and the information desks of Nanjing and Shanghai North stations. This announcement.

Joint Transportation Tickets 95

The tickets required for the joint transportation have been designed by the Traffic Department as a relatively simple perforated passenger ticket, which has been printed by the Accounting Department and distributed to the relevant stations, business offices, and the company for use. The Traffic Department has also sent a circular to the relevant personnel of each station and section, and stipulated that the joint transportation for children, whether on the railway or bus company side, shall be handled in accordance with Article 25 of the Passenger Transportation Regulations. All joint transportation tickets sold to children shall be collected at half the face value in accordance with the regulations.

Contract Summary 96

This joint transportation contract is very lengthy, so here is a summary: (1) The Railway Bureau will sell joint tickets at the following stations: Nanjing, Changzhou, Wuxi, Suzhou, and Shanghai. The Company will sell joint tickets at the following stations: Yangzhou and Shijiaqiao. Other stations can be gradually added as needed, with the agreement of both parties. Passengers traveling on the railway will be subject to the ticket grading system. The company does not classify tickets in that way. Tickets are valid for that day only. If the train for which the joint ticket was sold is delayed en route and cannot cross the river that day, the stationmaster or the company can sign and note it on the ticket, and it can be used the next day. (2) The Company's operating hours are from 6:40 a.m. to 5:50 p.m. daily. If any Railway Bureau trains are unable to arrive at Zhenjiang Railway Station by 5:30 p.m., the Railway Bureau's connecting stations cannot sell joint tickets. The Company's operating schedule mentioned above refers to the current schedule. If there are any changes in the future, the Company must notify them in advance. (3) The Company shall provide passenger vehicles to pick up and drop off passengers between the Company's pier and the Railway Bureau's station, charging each passenger $0.20. This fee will be included in the joint ticket price. (4) For the convenience of joint transportation, in addition to the original ferry facilities from Zhenjiang Pier to Liuwei, the Company will provide luggage vans from Liuwei to Yangzhou, and will also add passenger vehicles and luggage vans between Zhenjiang Pier and the station for connection. The Company is responsible for taking care of passengers' suitcases or packages weighing no more than 20 kilograms, with a transportation fee of $0.25 per piece. For those exceeding 20 kilograms, an additional fee of $0.10 will be charged for every 10 kilograms. Those less than 10 kilograms will be calculated as 10 kilograms. The company can refuse to transport those weighing up to 100 kilograms or those that are too bulky. Dangerous goods, contraband, perishable items, unclean items, carriages, livestock, fish, shrimp, etc., cannot be transported as luggage or packages. Valuables must be transported with insurance, and the insurance amount will be determined separately.

Sharp Decline in Overseas Sales of Chinese Silk 100

Total only two or three tenths of what it was before.

Silk factories are piled high with inventory and are shutting down one after another.

According to the New Sound News Agency, China's silk weaving industry has suffered a sharp decline in foreign trade due to the government's imposition of import duties on artificial silk and the impact of dumping by Japanese goods. Factories are shutting down one after another. Those that are struggling to maintain operations are only doing so by reducing working hours and lowering wages, just to maintain the current situation. The future is truly bleak.

Important Reasons 101

The silk fabrics produced by silk weaving factories are exported to foreign countries such as Southeast Asia and India, with an annual trade volume of about 18 million yuan. After the two increases in import duties on artificial silk in 1931 and 1932, the export of Chinese silk gradually decreased. Last year's exports totaled only two or three tenths of what they were before. In addition, Japanese goods are being dumped in Southeast Asia and India, making it difficult for Chinese silk to compete with Japanese goods in those areas. Chinese silk merchants' foreign trade is hesitant to move forward, regarding it as a daunting task. The recent months have seen the lowest level of Chinese silk exports ever. Moreover, Japanese artificial silk is not subject to tariffs, so its products can be dumped overseas. Artificial silk and silk are the most used materials for Chinese silk. Therefore, the use of silk has decreased accordingly.

State of Decline 102

There are a total of about 380 silk weaving factories in this city, with more than 4,800 looms, mostly in the Hongkou and Yangshupu areas. Now, due to the sharp decline in overseas sales of Chinese silk, inventory is piled up, production is excessive, and it is impossible to maintain operations. More than 20 factories have announced closures, such as Hongda Factory on Jumen Road, Taichangde on Tianbao Road, Minfeng Factory on Yangshupu Road, Meifeng Factory on Haizhou Road, and Yuanfeng Factory on Quren Road. Factories that have reduced wages include Hengfeng Factory on Pingliang Road, Wanbao Factory on Kangti Road, Baohua Factory on Yidingpan Road, as well as Yucun Factory and Jinxin Factory on Yangshupu Road, totaling more than 30 factories. As a result, labor disputes are rampant. The staff of the Mediation Section of the Social Affairs Bureau have been busy with mediation recently.

Sales of Chinese Tung Oil in Danger 103

The United States is experimenting with cultivation and increasing the amount of high-quality tung oil.

According to the Mainland Daily, the US Commercial Commissioner to China, Mr. Arnold, recently published an article on Chinese tung oil in a certain business newspaper. According to the article, tung oil has been a special product of China for hundreds of years. Because this product is a necessary ingredient in paint, 70% of China's tung oil exports are used by the US paint industry. If the supply can be uninterrupted, the US manufacturers will still import all of it from China. However, in 1921, the price of oil soared. In order to obtain a reliable supply, the US paint industry sought to produce this product domestically at a low price and high quality. The US Department of Agriculture had already experimented with planting tung trees in 1905, and now it is building on this foundation to seek development. Later, it gradually progressed, and its quality surpassed that of Chinese imports. This is because its refining method is superior to China's indigenous method. The tung oil produced in the United States is not only of good quality, but also its quantity is increasing day by day. This is because new uses have been discovered recently, so it is necessary to increase its production volume. The American planters should thank China for obtaining this profitable new industry. However, Chinese planters can also benefit from imitating the American refining method. The translator notes that everything in the world must be constantly improved in order to stand in an invincible position. China's silk and tea were originally major commodities for export, but their sales have been declining in recent years due to a lack of effort to improve manufacturing. Now, tung oil is repeating the same mistake. If urgent improvements are not made to compete with foreign goods, it is feared that in a few decades, China will also use imported tung oil for its own needs.

The Crisis of National Tea is Deepening Day by Day 104

Overseas sales of Chinese tea are decreasing year by year.

Sales in the Eastern Provinces have also become hopeless.

According to a report from the Shanghai Times' local office, in recent years, China's tea exports have been almost entirely plundered by tea from India, Ceylon, Java, Japan, and Taiwan. Overseas sales of Chinese tea are on the verge of crisis. Yesterday, a reporter from the Shanghai Times specifically inquired about the situation from the Commodity Inspection Bureau, the International Trade Bureau, and tea merchants, and the following is a summary of the information obtained:

Overseas Sales on the Verge of Crisis 105

In the past, tea was one of China's main exports. Recently, Chinese tea in overseas markets has been plundered by tea from Japan, India, and Ceylon. Chinese tea, which used to be the number one export in domestic trade, has now fallen to sixth place. The export volume has decreased by more than half when calculated over the past 60 years. The highest export volume of Chinese tea once reached more than 2 million dan per year, while tea exports in the last year (1933) were only slightly less than 700,000 dan, according to the Jianghai Customs report. The world's demand for tea has increased from 300 million pounds to 900 million pounds. This shows the decline in overseas sales of Chinese tea. The reason for this is that in recent decades, Japan, India, and Ceylon have had overproduction of tea and have implemented dumping policies. As a result, Chinese tea has been greatly affected. In addition, the global economic recession and China's internal unrest, poor agricultural harvests, and reduced production have further endangered overseas sales of national tea.

Chinese Tea Disappears in the Northeast 106

The tea consumed annually in the four northeastern provinces used to be transported from Fujian, Jiangsu, and Zhejiang to various parts of the four provinces for distribution, amounting to 5 million catties per year, worth more than 4 million yuan. Since the September 18th Incident, the northeastern market has been completely seized by the Japanese puppets. In September of the year before last, the puppet state increased the import ad valorem tax on tea by 30%. As a result, Chinese tea, which used to monopolize the northeastern market, has fallen into a desperate situation. Japanese and Taiwanese tea took advantage of the decline of Chinese tea and monopolized sales in the Eastern Provinces. From May to the end of last year, about 2 million catties of Taiwanese tea were imported, worth 2 million yuan. As a result, the sales of Chinese tea in the three northeastern provinces have completely disappeared.

Tea Fields Lie Fallow, Tea Warehouses Close 107

In recent years, due to the decline in the tea market and the impact of financial tightening, inland tea warehouses have closed one after another. For example, in the two places of Wuyuan and Tunxi in Anhui, there were more than 300 tea warehouses that produced tea, but now only a few dozen can operate. In addition, of the 81 counties in Jiangxi Province, 50 counties produce tea. In recent years, due to the daily decline in overseas sales and the frequent ravages of the bandits, tea merchants have regarded operating in the tea industry as a daunting task, causing farmers who make a living by planting tea to abandon tea fields and seek other means of production because they have nowhere to sell the tea they produce. In most tea-producing areas across the country, tea gardens are left to lie fallow.

Industry Authorities Discuss Relief 108

The crisis of national tea is deepening day by day. If it is not rescued quickly, not only will the overseas market be lost, but foreign tea will have a tendency to be imported. In a few years, national tea will be in danger of a fundamental collapse. It is learned that the Ministry of Industry has paid attention to this and has decided to revitalize the Chinese tea industry in order to remedy the situation. It has also issued orders to the agricultural administration authorities in various provinces to supervise farmers to work hard to plant tea, and to establish experimental farms in major tea areas to improve planting in the immediate vicinity, in order to improve the tea industry. It is also seeking to establish direct sales agencies abroad to avoid exploitation by foreign firms, in order to reduce costs and compete with Japanese tea and other teas to restore the glory of Chinese tea in the past.

Red Korean Spies Said to Be Planning to Attack the Japanese Consulate General 109

According to the Japanese Shanghai Daily yesterday, the clandestine activities of red elements on North Sichuan Road in the city have become increasingly fierce recently. A few days ago, they even distributed unstable Japanese texts to the Japanese Navy. In addition, the Three L's Commemorative Week and the January 28th Anniversary are approaching, and it is rumored that unstable activities are underway. Three red Koreans who secretly came to Shanghai from Nanjing a few days ago are responsible for the guidance among the Koreans in Shanghai. They aim to achieve Korean independence and are in contact with the communist party. They plan to take advantage of the January 28th Anniversary to launch an attack on the Japanese Consulate General. Therefore, the police of the Consulate General have increased personnel and are on serious alert inside and outside the building in order to prevent any unexpected events. At the same time, they are working with the inspectors of the Public Works Department to defend the area near the Consulate General.

The Ministry of Transportation's Second Examination of Chinese and Foreign Seafarers 117

Held on the 24th of this month

118 examinees

In order to implement maritime safety, the Ministry of Transportation is conducting examinations of Chinese and foreign seafarers in accordance with the Provisional Regulations on Seafarer Examinations in order to distinguish them. Those who do not take the examination will have their original qualifications cancelled. The date of the second examination of Chinese and foreign seafarers has been set for 8:00 a.m. on the 24th of this month at the Wusong Merchant Marine School in Shanghai. A total of 118 people are scheduled to take the examination this time. The Ministry of Transportation has specially appointed Gao Tingzi to come to Shanghai to supervise the examination. The examination subjects and the list of examinees are recorded as follows:

Examination Subjects: All examinees must bring a recent 2.5-inch photo and all necessary stationery to the examination location at 8:00 a.m. on the 24th. The examination subjects include two types: deck officers and engine officers. Deck officers are divided into (1) compass, (2) naval architecture, (3) navigation (including astronomical calculations), (4) navigation collision avoidance methods, (5) semaphore signals, (6) pilotage, (7) charts, (8) maritime law, (9) English, (10) mathematics. Engine officers are divided into (1) drawing, (2) materials, (3) mechanics, (4) pressure, (5) principles of steam.

British Gunboat to Conduct Cannon Tests Today 119

At Langshan and Tongsha, etc.

The British Yangtze River shallow-water gunboat Ludy Bird [Nadbo] is scheduled to conduct cannon tests on the waters of Tongsha and Nantong Langshan outside the Wusongkou on both today and tomorrow. Yesterday, the British naval commander in China sent a letter to the headquarters of the Navy Training Fleet to request that they take note and inform the residents near the above-mentioned two places that there is no need to panic at that time.

Xin Sheng She said that the Shanghai-Ningbo route of the Sanbei Company's Small Sanbei steamer, the expulsion of the middle cabin workers' dispute, the middle cabin association, convened an emergency delegates meeting yesterday to discuss how to deal with the matter. The details are as follows:

Exported Yesterday Morning The Small Sanbei Steamer, the route was changed five times the day before yesterday, and the middle cabin workers were expelled by the company. The Seamen's Union, fearing a bloodshed, negotiated and temporarily ordered 16 workers to leave the ship, while the remaining 15 workers continued to serve on the ship. In addition, the company added six new workers who had not joined the union to work on the ship. The ship was exported yesterday morning. Due to the union's many obstacles, all the old workers were allowed to handle the matter, and no incidents occurred. However, everyone was extremely resentful.

Delegates Meeting The Seamen's Middle Cabin Association, with the case of the British-produced Swire Company's Wusong ship not yet resolved, this company is now trying to follow suit, which is intentionally destroying the labor movement. Chaired by Wang Min, the meeting discussed and decided to submit a request to the Seamen's Party Department, the Seamen's Union, and the Seamen's Branch to negotiate according to law and seek a solution as soon as possible. The Seamen's Union will hold a meeting on February 1 to discuss the entire reorganization of the middle cabin.

Mr. Yu Returns to Shanghai In order to avoid the expansion of the situation, the Seamen's Union has temporarily decided on a transitional method of half the work, and will discuss a solution after the company's manager, Yu Qiaqing, returns to Shanghai. It is now known that Mr. Yu has returned to Shanghai from Beijing today. The union has decided to negotiate with the company tomorrow to establish a permanent method. However, the workers stated that if the union cannot resolve the matter, they will not hesitate to make any sacrifices when the ship arrives in Shanghai on the 30th to deal with the company. Workers' Representatives from the Samsung Yarn Factory

Declared Hunger Strike Yesterday 129

Demanding the Return of Workers' Savings

To Petition the Party and Government This Morning

Da Gong She reported that the Samsung Yarn Factory on Yangshupu Road in East Shanghai was founded by Sheng Xingxun, Minister of Posts and Communications of the late Qing Dynasty, and has been in operation for more than 50 years, with a wide scope and employing more than 4,000 workers. These workers have an organization called the Tongshan Association, and each worker donates two days' wages each year. Over the years, the amount has reached more than 500,000 yuan, and the funds are handled by the factory manager, Sheng Yujun, stored in the bank, and a lot of real estate has been purchased in the Yangshupu area. In 1930, the factory was sold to the Shenxin No. 9 Factory, but the workers' savings have not yet been returned. A lawsuit was filed in court, and the court ordered Sheng Yujun to pay 120,000 to ensure his release. However, the lawsuit has not yet been judged, causing panic among the workers. After discussion, it was decided to seek a final solution to seek social justice.

Declared Hunger Strike 130

The workers elected representatives to repeatedly demand that Sheng Yujun return the savings, but there was still no result. The workers believed that such a delay meant that the workers' representatives had other intentions, and severely criticized them. In order to prove their innocence, the representatives carried bedding to Sheng Yujun's residence at No. 122, Western Alley, Xinxingli, Tiantong Road at 7:00 AM yesterday and declared a hunger strike to seek a final solution. The workers on hunger strike include Gu Lansheng, Zeng Songshan, Lu Zhida, Ding Zhuting, Lu Wenbin, Sheng Zhongheng, Liu Binghai, and seven others.

Request for Assistance 131

After the workers' representatives, Gu Lansheng and others, declared a hunger strike, the other workers decided to prepare a petition at 10:00 AM this morning and go to the Municipal Party Department, the Social Affairs Bureau, the General Labor Union, and other agencies to request that personnel be sent to thoroughly investigate so that the savings handled by Sheng Yujun can be returned in full, otherwise they vowed not to eat again.

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Writes to the Public Works Department to Strive for the Longan Industry Not to Be Subject to Miscellaneous License Fees 137

Forty-Six Industries Jointly Assist

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, for the new miscellaneous taxes created by the Health Department of the Public Concession Engineering Bureau, forcing the Longan industry to obtain food donation licenses, specially wrote to the Engineering Bureau to strive for exemption from paying the license. The original text is recorded as follows: Dear Sirs, On the 19th of this month, according to the Shanghai Dried Fragrant Longan Industry Association, as well as the postal transport industry, the coal industry, and other forty-six industry associations, they jointly stated in a letter that, according to a joint letter from 13 members including Rongchun, etc., our stores are opened on Fujian Road, and the oldest brand has been around for more than 50 years, and the next oldest is more than 10 years. (There are account books and house tax receipts as proof) There has never been a precedent for needing to donate licenses with cooked food stores. However, in November 1927 and July 1932, the Health Department of the Public Concession Engineering Bureau wanted to collect food donations from our stores, and they were all exempted after requesting the Chinese Taxpayers Association to argue on the basis of reason and the court to uphold justice. There are old cases to be checked. According to the first special district court of July 25, 1932, when Judge Shen of the Liao Police Court heard the case, he said that the Engineering Bureau's lawsuit against Rongchun Yongchun and other stores for violating regulations did not apply to Article 34 of the Yangjingbang. If they want to order the store to obtain a license, they must revise the Yangjingbang regulations before there is a basis. Judge Shen upheld justice and protected the rights of Chinese businessmen, and his merits are truly praiseworthy. The Engineering Bureau has repeatedly sued for seven years, hearing no less than dozens of courts. Our stores have repeatedly protested, denying the donation, embracing the spirit of unyielding struggle, fearing that it would affect the rights of the entire Chinese merchants in the country and the concession. Last year, the Health Department of the Engineering Bureau again sued our stores in the first local court of the special zone for opening food stores on Fujian Road on April 10, June 23, July 28, and November 30 without donating licenses to the Health Department, claiming that it violated regulations, which is inconsistent with the facts, because the items sold by our stores are mostly sandalwood and longan and other raw dried fruits, and other items such as walnuts and lychees do not interfere with hygiene. According to Article 34 of the Yangjingbang regulations, teahouses, restaurants, dance halls, storytelling venues, etc. must donate licenses, that is, the Chinese food sale shop license of the Engineering Bureau, which explains that this license is applicable to all shops selling fresh meat, fresh fish, poultry, vegetables, and cooked food. Judging from this, it can be clearly understood that our stores are not cooked food stores at all, nor are they food stores. The so-called cooked food store refers to customers eating in the store, not buying out. Then the goods sold by our stores are fundamentally different from food stores and cooked food stores. The Health Department's lawsuit for violating regulations is obviously unfounded. It is difficult to acknowledge that such harsh donations disturb merchants and illegal oppression. When Judge Deng of the First Special District Court heard the case on December 15 last year, he did not examine the regulations of Article 34 of the Yangjingbang and ordered a fine of 10 yuan and a supplementary donation, which was to despise the merchants and arbitrarily impose fines and supplementary donations. It is difficult to be satisfied. In addition to filing an appeal, we specially request your association to approve the transfer of the letter to the Chamber of Commerce and negotiate with the Engineering Bureau to cancel it, etc. After checking the above-mentioned sections on the right, they are indeed true. It is unfortunate that the store has been oppressed by this newly created harsh donation, and it is even more difficult to be convinced by the unfounded penalties of the court. In this time of commercial depression, how can it be allowed to be arbitrarily demanded and slaughtered without end? If we do not unite and strive, our small and weak merchants will have no survivors. Approving the letter and the reasons for it, we urgently join all trade associations to write a letter requesting your association to approve the transfer of the letter to the Public Concession Engineering Bureau to negotiate on the basis of reason to cancel the harsh donations, and ask the Chinese directors to assist in the struggle to relieve the difficulties and pain of merchants. According to this, after checking this case in September of last year, according to the same situation as before, after transferring the letter to your bureau for review and cancellation, you replied that the engineering bureau has the right to order this food shop to obtain a license according to the concession regulations, etc. However, after careful examination of Article 34 of the Yangjingbang Concession Regulations, the shops and venues that should be licensed are listed, and the shops not listed do not need to be licensed. It is certainly not possible to use the word "right" to force a license indefinitely. The items sold in sandalwood longan shops are mostly made through exquisite procedures, and there has never been a hygiene problem. It can be seen that they cannot be licensed. It is inevitable to have an abuse of power to charge a fee for native product stores that should not be licensed. The corresponding letter will continue to be sent according to the situation, and we hope that your bureau will check that the sandalwood longan store is not listed in Article 34 of the Yangjingbang Concession Regulations, and will not be forced to pay a license. It is deeply appreciated.

Tongzhou Waterway Light Vessel Moved 139

The Hydrographic Survey Bureau issued a navigation announcement yesterday, stating that the azimuth of the light buoy pile of the Tongzhou Waterway light vessel at the mouth of the Yangtze River on the east coast of the Republic of China has moved, and a new light buoy pile has been set up, which will be replaced on January 23. The moving positions are: (1) The azimuth of the light vessel has moved, the new azimuth is 166 degrees north of the Tongzhou Customs clock tower, a distance of 2.66 nautical miles, that is, about 120 degrees 46 minutes east longitude and about 31 degrees 59 minutes north latitude. Note that the Tongzhou light vessel will be moved to the new azimuth on the above date, and its nature remains the same. (2) The azimuth of the light buoy pile has moved, the new azimuth is 161 degrees north of the Tongzhou Customs clock tower, a distance of 3.19 nautical miles, that is, about 120 degrees 46 minutes east longitude and about 31 degrees 59 minutes north latitude. Note that the Qingtian Reef light buoy pile will be moved to the new azimuth on the above date, and its nature remains the same. (3) Set up a new light buoy pile, azimuth 152 degrees north of the Tongzhou Customs clock tower, a distance of 1.89 nautical miles, that is, about 120 degrees 47 minutes east longitude and about 31 degrees 59 minutes north latitude. Abbreviated flashing every three seconds, explanation, red conical buoy pile, equipped with a white flashing light, cycle of three seconds, flashing for 0.3 seconds, dark for 2.7 seconds. Note that this buoy pile is named Tongzhou Waterway Light Buoy Pile.

Xu Zhenya and the Counter-Romance of Laughter and Tears 142

Xu Denies Ever Writing This Book

Accuses Jin Wentang Owner of Fraud

Xu Zhenya, owner of Qinghua Bookstore on Jiaotong Road, is a prolific writer. However, his works are published by his own bookstore. Recently, the Jin Wentang Bookstore published a novel called [Counter-Romance of Laughter and Tears], which listed Xu as the author. After seeing it, Xu believed that he did not want to take credit for others' work, so he hired lawyer Yang Ruinian to sue Li Dingchen, owner of Jin Wentang Bookstore, for harming his reputation and defrauding money in the First Special District Court, stating that the defendant had arbitrarily added his name to the list of authors of the book and published advertisements in various newspapers to promote it as much as possible. The plaintiff is a literary man who has always respected morality and valued his reputation. He has never met the defendant, so how can he write and publish it? He does not know what kind of book the Counter-Romance of Laughter and Tears is. If the content is good, he dares not take credit for it. If the content is bad, he is even more unwilling to share the blame for others. Only name and instrument cannot be faked. The defendant never notified him before or after the incident. His behavior is tantamount to theft. He not only harmed the plaintiff's credit with fraud, but also used illegal means to defraud the money of book buyers. In order to achieve the purpose of defrauding money, he also published advertisements in various newspapers, saying that the old talent was desperately fighting for fame, and there were slogans guaranteeing how this book was with the plaintiff's reputation. The plaintiff's previous works were numerous, and their quality has its own evaluation, but there has been no writing in recent years, and the defendant actually used the Counter-Romance of Laughter and Tears, written by someone else, for the plaintiff to desperately fight for fame, and actually publicly insulted him. The defendant's behavior before and after constituted the crime of harming reputation and credit in Article 330 and Article 324 of the Criminal Law. The plaintiff has always made a living by writing and publishing, but now he has been given a book of incongruous nature, Li Dai Zhang Guan, his reputation has been damaged, and his business has also been sharply reduced. The future losses are endless. For this reason, he filed a civil lawsuit incidentally, hoping that the defendant will be summoned to court as soon as possible and sentenced to the crime he deserves, and ordered to compensate for damages of 20,000 yuan. After being sued, Li Dingchen also hired a lawyer to file a statement to defend himself, and implicated the novelist Xu Zheshen, saying that the Counter-Romance of Laughter and Tears was originally introduced by Xu, and Xu was paid a fee. Therefore, he filed a lawsuit against Xu Zheshen for fraud. On Saturday afternoon, Judge Zhan Liangce of the First Special Court opened a court to summon and question the three plaintiffs and defendants, but none of them came in person. Lawyer Yang briefly stated the case, and Li Dingchen's lawyer requested that the two cases be consolidated for trial, because they are the same fact, and combined trials are easier to understand and save time. The court agreed to the request and ordered both parties to come to court again at 3:00 PM next month for questioning.

Page 11

Public Groups and Public Banquets in This City for Dr. Marek 143

Public Lecture at Wuben Girls' High School in the Afternoon

Denmark is an Ideal Country for Us

My Country Should Learn From This to Revitalize the Countryside

Dr. Marek, an expert in adult education from Denmark and the Dean of the International People's College, visited China and gave a lecture at the Jiangsu Provincial College of Education in Wuxi. Yesterday, the Municipal Education Bureau and various groups in this city held a public banquet for Dr. Marek at the Bank Club at 12:00 noon. In the afternoon at 4:00 PM, he gave a public lecture at Wuben Girls' High School. The details are as follows:

Public Banquet 144

The groups participating in the public banquet included Director Pan of the Municipal Education Bureau, Chen Bai, Zhou Feicheng, Hu Shuyi, Zhou Shang, Huang Zaoxiong of the Municipal Education Association, Xu Zeyu, Ma Jiazhen, Kang Xuanyi of the University Education Association, Ma Gongyu of the Chinese Academy of Arts and Sciences, Huang Renzhi of the Vocational Education Association, Jiang Wenyu, Pan Yangyao, Yang Weiyu, He Qingru, Xu Xingchu of the International Society, Xu Zexiang of the Chinese Education Association, Chen Jicheng, Cao Yunxiang of the International Affairs Research Association, Chen Songchun of the Citizens' Education Center, Yang Minshi of the Shanghai Branch of the Film Association, Lu Shibai, Gu Xuchu of the Shenbao Amateur Tutoring School, Liao Maoru of Guanghua High School, and more than 50 others. Director Pan, the chairman, first gave a brief introduction, followed by Dr. Marek's speech.

Mr. Ma's Speech 145

He briefly stated, "I am very honored to be invited here today. Denmark's central position makes it highly suitable for international harmony. Currently, Denmark's folk high schools educate one-fourth of the entire population. Some believe that Danish folk high schools have a very strong sense of nationalism, but this is not necessarily a virtue of the folk high schools. Danish folk high schools were founded during the Romantic era when nationalism was prevalent, so the schools were naturally influenced by this. However, the unique characteristic of Danish folk high schools lies in their emphasis on teacher-student collaboration and the integration of language and emotion. The Danish philosopher Bishop Grundtvig once said, 'Language is the highest expression of personality and vitality.' Although he did not emphasize literature, the fact that almost all Danish farmers are now literate is due to the inspiration and guidance of language education. The purpose of the Danish folk high school curriculum is not to meet vocational needs, but to enable people to return to their original environment and engage in improvement. Folk education is not about testing students, but about answering their questions. Grundtvig also believed that children, while still innocent, should not be burdened with heavy educational materials. Therefore, during the ages of fourteen to eighteen, they should not be subjected to political education. Only after eighteen is it appropriate to implement national education, because at this time, young people become interested in various issues and should be guided to seek answers from history."

Danish Folk Education 146

"Its purpose is not only to improve the country, but also to promote international peace. The International People's College, which I run, was founded with this mission. When it was first established, it was very simple, but now it has gradually flourished, with about 120 students from various countries. However, people from different countries have different national characteristics and different attitudes towards education. We have made every effort to get them to cooperate, and now everyone can be educated under the same curriculum, and their feelings are also harmonious, like a small league of nations. Generally speaking, if international organizations lack sincere cooperation from various countries and harbor mutual animosity, they will never be successful. In fact, no country can boast that its own civilization includes all the advantages of mankind. Each country has its own strengths, so the first step is mutual understanding, and then the realization of a truly harmonious world can be expected."

Public Lecture 147

At 4:00 p.m., Mr. Ma gave a public lecture in the auditorium of Wuben Girls' Middle School, attended by more than 500 people. The chairman, Director Pan, gave an introduction, followed by the lecture, translated by Liao Maoru. The topic was ["Danish Folk High Schools and the Prosperity of Rural Society"]. Mr. Ma spoke fluent English with clear articulation and was truly a skilled speaker. The general idea was that the Danish national character is rational, and people are willing to work hard and not engage in empty talk. Farmers are literate and can apply scientific knowledge. The rural environment is particularly poetic and truly an ideal country for us. He then spoke about Denmark's land policy and cooperative undertakings.] Denmark has reached the point where tillers own their land, and the countryside is quite wealthy, so our country can use Denmark as a reference for revitalizing the countryside. After the lecture, lantern slides were shown to illustrate the situation in Danish folk high schools. Afterwards, the Shanghai branch of the Educational Film Association screened educational films, and the event ended at about 7:00 p.m.

Shipwreck in the Huangpu River 148

Hydrographic Survey Bureau Issues Notice on Navigational Boundary

The Hydrographic Survey Bureau of the Naval Department issued a notice regarding the destruction of a shipwreck in the Huangpu River near Shanghai and the removal of a lighted buoy, urging ships to pay attention to the navigational boundary.

"He'an" Shipwreck Location: In the new waterway of Gaoqiao Sand in the Huangpu River. Bearing: 101 degrees due north from the water tower of the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company. Distance: 1.44 nautical miles. That is, approximately 121 degrees 33 minutes East longitude and 31 degrees 20 minutes North latitude. The notice stated that the "He'an" ship has been destroyed, and the symbol on the chart should be deleted.

Lighted Buoy Location: 75 feet northeast of the above-mentioned (1) shipwreck. The notice stated that the lighted buoy marking the shipwreck has also been removed.

Fisheries Guidance Center Announces Fisheries Production and Sales Situation for Last Month 149

Salted Fish Sales Stagnant, Fresh Fish Sales Booming

Mostly Japanese Goods in Marine Products Import

The fisheries situation in this city has always lacked precise statistics. Since the establishment of the Fisheries Guidance Center in this city, personnel have been dispatched to various fisheries markets every day to investigate the production and sales situation, and systematic records have begun to be kept. The production and sales situation of the fish market in this city for December of last year has been compiled and is excerpted below.

Reduced Imports 150

According to reports, the total import volume of fish in this city in December of last year was 78,326 dan and 14 jin, a decrease of 19,391 dan and 68 jin compared with the previous month. The total value was 1,453,568.04 yuan, a decrease of 309,978.88 yuan compared with the previous month.

Booming Sales 151

As for the sales of various fish, in addition to a decrease in salted fish sales, the sales of iced fresh fish all increased. Marine Products Imports 152

Strict Prohibition of Preparing Lawsuits on Behalf of Others, No Soliciting Extortion 153

Order from the Ministry of Justice

To be followed by all courts in this city.

The First and Second Special District Courts, the Jiangsu High Court Branch, and the District Court in this city received an order from the Ministry of Justice yesterday, stating: "It has been found that many courts and prosecutor's offices in various provinces have established lawsuit writing offices, selected lawsuit writers to prepare lawsuits or legal documents on behalf of litigants, and formulated rules to be followed. This is extremely convenient for litigants who cannot write or are illiterate, and also prevents lawsuit brokers from monopolizing cases. The law is not flawed, but as it has been implemented for a long time, abuses have gradually emerged. Recently, it has been heard that these lawsuit writing offices either demand more than the fees that should be charged or try to force people to have them prepare lawsuits on their behalf in order to collect fees. If their demands are not met, they inevitably deliberately create difficulties, causing endless harm to the litigants, or delaying deadlines as a result. This situation, if serious, violates criminal law, and even if minor, clearly violates laws and regulations, harming both the rights of the people and the prestige of the court. It should be strictly investigated and prevented from becoming a source of abuse. Therefore, all courts should thoroughly investigate whether the courts or prosecutor's offices under their jurisdiction have lawsuit writing offices or similar organizations, and whether they have the above-mentioned situations. They should be rectified and not allow laws intended to benefit the people to turn into harms."

Local Yellow Wine Industry Association

Resolution on This Year's Rice Price Standard for Winemaking 154

The Local Yellow Wine Industry Association held a members' meeting the day before yesterday, chaired by Fang Zhongheng. The matters discussed are recorded below: (1) Discussion on what standard should be used for the price of each grade of rice for winemaking this year. Resolution: Regardless of contract brewing or self-brewing, the standard for each grade of rice is 14 shi and 7.5 dou. Each shi is calculated at 6.92 yuan, totaling 102.07 yuan. Each grade of wine is released for sale with a weight of 4,620 jin. This calculation is based on a discount of 848 from the former Haihu. (2) Discussion on the issue of tax registration for the industry. Resolution: The wine produced and stored by the industry should be registered in accordance with the regulations. However, if the brewed wine is sold to other ports, and inferior wine is found after it arrives at that port, the workshop, because the wine storage vessels were sealed in advance, may not know it themselves. Therefore, if there is an opening of an inferior wine can, the tax authorities should explain and guarantee that the brewer is not responsible. Furthermore, the registration should be based on a 90% standard (for example, 90 cans should be registered for 100 cans). After the registration form is filled out with the quantity and sealed, it should be sent to the association, which will compile it and report it to the tax authorities for record.

Court Judgment in the Ji Juemi Case 155

Xin Xin News Agency reports that the case of Ji Jueer being accused of seduction by Xu Yuying has been judged by the court. Ji Juemi and Yu Xiaomei were declared not guilty. The reasoning of the judgment is as follows: The main point of the prosecution is that on May 17 of this year (22nd year of the Republic), the defendants Ji Juemi and Yu Xiaomei seduced the plaintiff to Li's residence at No. 101 Cihou North Lane, Hadong Road, for fornication. On the 3rd day of the intercalary 5th month, they continued to fornicate at the Hongkou Hotel, with clothes, photos, and hospital records as evidence. The defendants are guilty of Article 240, Paragraph 2, and Article 244, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Code, etc. After the court hearing, the plaintiff's statements were mostly inconsistent with the indictment. (1) In court, she stated that Yu Xiaomei invited her to No. 101 Cihou North Lane, which is inconsistent with the indictment, which stated that Ji Juemi invited her. (2) In court, she stated that the fornication at that place occurred on May 12, which is inconsistent with the indictment, which stated May 17. (3) In court, she stated that she went to the Hongkou Hotel at 1:30 p.m. on the 3rd day of the intercalary 5th month, which is inconsistent with the indictment, which stated 6:00 p.m. (4) In court, she stated that Ji Juemi left the hotel more than two hours after the fornication at the hotel, and did not return until 9:00 a.m. the next morning, which is inconsistent with the indictment, which stated that she stayed at the hotel that night and continued to be fornicated. These are the facts claimed by the plaintiff herself, and the statements are obviously inconsistent, which is already cause for suspicion. The defendants all denied any seduction or continued fornication. Regarding the plaintiff's claim that she was given a set of clothes by Li Ziyu's wife after being fornicated at Li's residence at No. 101 Cihou North Lane, the court investigated and learned from Li Ziyu that Ji Juemi and Xu Yuying had never been to that place, and that he had not yet married a wife, so where would the woman's clothes come from? It is clear that the plaintiff's claim of fornication at Li's residence is untrue. As for the claim of continued fornication at the Hongkou Hotel and the gift of a photo from Ji Juemi, Ji Juemi strongly denied it, claiming that the photo was taken of him wearing mourning clothes with a memorial badge, which was originally published in the Hadong Rong'ailu and was widely available, making it easy to reprint. The court inspected the photos submitted by the plaintiff and found that they did not have Ji Juemi's signature or the photographer's studio. The clothing (mourning clothes with a memorial badge), clothing marks, and background patterns were no different from those published in the Rong'ailu. Although the plaintiff's agent, Gong Wenhuan, stated that the photos submitted by the plaintiff had two collars, which were different from the photos in the Rong'ailu, a close examination revealed that there was only a black line between the collars, not two collars. This black line could be easily added during reprinting and is not sufficient evidence that the defendant gave it. Moreover, the Shanghai Shangbao had already published this photo before the filing of this case, as can be seen from the court's case file No. 607 of the 22nd year of the Republic. The Shanghai Morning Post (December 23, 22nd year of the Republic) also published the same photo during the proceedings of this case, which further proves that the defendant's claim that this kind of photo was widely available and easy to reprint is credible. Although the waiter Xue Quanyuan stated that the person who opened room No. 8 at the Hongkou Hotel on June 25 (i.e., the 3rd day of the intercalary 5th month) was the defendant Ji Juemi, the hotel's register clearly stated that room No. 8 was for Li Zheng, 38 years old, from Guangdong, which is obviously inconsistent with the witness's testimony. Moreover, it has been half a year since June 25, the day of the court hearing. The witness is responsible for many as four rooms, and there is frequent traffic of guests. It is strange that the witness was able to remember every detail about the guest in room No. 8 on that day, such as their age, accent, when they opened the room, when the female guest came, when the guest left, when they returned, how much the room cost, and so on. Considering the circumstances of the reprinted photo, the defendant's accusation of falsehood is not without reason. As for the plaintiff's claim of going to the hospital for a diagnosis, since the alleged fornication is unfounded, there is no need to study it. Regarding the testimony of Zhang Danqing of Jishan Hospital, his diagnosis of the plaintiff was on May 14, which is inconsistent with the plaintiff's indictment, which stated that the fornication occurred on May 17. Zhou Hongzhang's diagnosis at the Red Cross Hospital on the 3rd day of the sixth month was that she had taken a small amount of ["Lysol"], and the reason for taking it was unknown. The testimonies of these two witnesses are not sufficient to corroborate the defendants' commission of fornication in this case. Based on the above, the plaintiff's case is clearly unprovable, and the defendants should be declared not guilty. Therefore, the plaintiff's age is irrelevant. Furthermore, Lin Ji, the director of the Institute of Forensic Medicine, certified that the plaintiff was over 17 years old, so there is no doubt that the defendants did not constitute a crime. Based on the above conclusions, the judgment is made in accordance with Articles 357 and 316 of the Criminal Procedure Law as follows:

New Pharmaceutical Industry Association

Notice on Changing to the New System of Weights and Measures 157

The New Pharmaceutical Industry Association of this city sent a letter to its members yesterday regarding the change to the new system of weights and measures, stating: "Dear Members, We have recently received an order from the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau stating that the National Bureau of Weights and Measures of the Ministry of Industry has inquired that Western medicines previously mostly used the British system, but recently many have adopted the standard system. However, the British system is still often mixed in. When using the standard system, Japanese and old translations are often used, such as calling centimeters grams or grams, cubic centimeters cc, and liters liter, which do not conform to the legally mandated names of the new system and are inappropriate. In the future, all Western medicine businesses must follow the unit names stipulated in Articles 4 and 6 of the Weights and Measures Law and Articles 52 and 53 of its implementation rules in order to comply with laws and regulations. In addition to separate inquiries, we also inquired about checking and forwarding the original articles of Articles 4 and 6 of the Weights and Measures Law and Articles 52 and 53 of its implementation rules, so that the association can forward them to all colleagues for compliance. We are attaching the original document printed and sealed and look forward to your pharmacy implementing it in accordance with these laws and regulations."
