Pan Xulun's Lecture 160

Experiences in Improving Factory Accounting 161

Yesterday, the China Industrial and Commercial Management Association specially invited accounting expert Pan Xulun to give a lecture on experiences in improving factory accounting at the Lianhua General Association. More than 40 people attended, including Ji Jiannan, Li Zhaohuan, Shen Jiucheng, Xu Yongzuo, Pan Yangyao, Hu Xiyuan, Fang Jiange, Cao Yunxiang, and Sheng Zhuosan. The lecture was recorded by personnel sent by Bingxun Stenography Agency. The main points were (1) Factories in our country do not have established standards for valuing inventory and depreciation, resulting in the loss of effectiveness of ordinary accounting. (2) It is still not possible to talk about adopting cost accounting in our country because of high costs and a lack of personnel. Therefore, it is best to use a permanent inventory system for bookkeeping and estimate the number of semi-finished products at the end of each month, which will almost cover the effectiveness of cost accounting. (3) For the accounting personnel in factories in our country, it is advisable to select young employees from the factory and send them to tutoring schools to learn, which is both economical and much better than hiring school graduates who are out of touch with the actual situation.

Investigation of a Case of Private Prostitute Falling to Her Death

Letter Requesting Punishment of Western Police Officer On-site 162

Gan Zhigang's Letter to the Public Works Department

Police Officer Peier of the Old Gate Police Station, together with Chinese police officer Xu A Jin No. 642, went to the third floor of the Longfei Shoe Store on Zhejiang Road on the 5th of this month to investigate private prostitution, resulting in the tragic death of Wang Xiuzhen after falling from the building. Later, Gan Zhigang surrendered, stating that the deceased was his wife, and hired lawyer Wang Buyuan to file a criminal lawsuit against Xu A Jin with the First Special District Court, requesting punishment according to law. However, the police station determined that Wang Xiuzhen was actually a private prostitute. The case has been tried once by the Special Court, and the details have been reported in previous newspapers. Now, Gan Zhigang believes that since the Chinese police officer has already been prosecuted, he should wait for the court to make a judgment. However, at the same time, he feels that it is unfair that the Western police officer on-site is still not involved. Therefore, he hired lawyer Wang as a representative to send a letter to the Police Department of the Public Works Department, requesting that the Western police officer be dealt with fairly. The letter is as follows: "Dear Editors, I am writing to inform you that the party concerned, Gan Zhigang, and his mother-in-law, Wang Guo Shi, claim that his wife, Gan Wang Shi (i.e., Wang Xiuzhen), lived in the back room on the third floor of the Feilong Shoe Store at No. 431 Zhejiang Road. Gan Zhigang runs a rice store and leaves early and returns late. At around 5 p.m. on the 5th of this month, the Police Officer Peier of the Old Gate Police Station, together with Chinese police officer Xu A Jin No. 642, suddenly broke into the house, went upstairs, and knocked on the door. The civilian's wife, Xiuzhen, immediately opened the door. The police officer did not explain the reason and immediately slapped her in the face. The civilian's wife saw that they were very fierce, and her explanation was ineffective. The Chinese police officer, without asking questions, punched and kicked her. The Chinese police officer Xu A Jin was so violent. My mother-in-law tried to help, and the civilian's wife was grabbed and brutally beaten by the Western police officer. The civilian's wife was a young and weak woman who was innocently subjected to this brutality. In a very anxious situation, she shouted for help on the street from the window. The Chinese police officer Xu A Jin was extremely violent and ran forward to punch her, causing my wife to fall onto the cement platform on the second floor. At that time, her head was down and her feet were up, causing her brain to rupture and die on the spot. The situation of the civilian's wife's tragic death is indescribable. The Chinese police officer Xu A Jin knew that he had caused a disaster and, of course, his power was slightly reduced. However, the Western police officer was still on-site when the incident occurred, and did not stop it. After the disaster, he released my mother-in-law. Although there were private prostitutes such as Li Qiaozhen living in the front building, it had nothing to do with Zhigang. After the police officer entered the house, he did not ask the reason and immediately beat anyone he saw. Granted that prostitutes and private prostitutes have committed crimes, but according to the law, they are only guilty of violating police regulations. Arresting prostitutes is not comparable to arresting thieves. The two prostitutes Li Qiaozhen and Wang Jinfeng were both in the front building at the time and did not go out to solicit customers. The police officer should not have entered the house to search without authorization. According to our country's criminal procedure law, in addition to flagrant offenders or defendants who have been detained, people's homes may not be searched without reason. Although Li Qiaozhen and others were prostitutes, they were sitting at home and did not go out to solicit customers, so they were not flagrant offenders. The two police officers entered people's homes without authorization without detention or search documents, which is a violation of the law. After entering the house, they did not explain the reason or investigate clearly who was good or bad, and beat anyone they saw. The civilian's wife and mother-in-law repeatedly explained to them, but the police officer ignored them and beat them both. The civilian's wife was forced to retreat to the front room. The Chinese police officer chased after her. In a desperate situation, she called for help from the window, but the police officer punched her, causing her to fall to the second floor, where she was seriously injured and died. Xu A Jin's nature is inherently violent. The Western police officer, as the head, should have been careful in handling the matter when exercising his duties. The Chinese police officer killed an innocent person, and he is responsible beyond any doubt. The Western police officer is also difficult to shirk his responsibility. A lawsuit has already been filed against the Chinese police officer Xu A Jin, and the Western police officer Peier did not stop Xu A Jin's illegal actions, and his fault cannot be excused. Please ask your lawyers to jointly represent us and send a letter to the Police Department of the Public Works Department for a fair investigation in order to protect the people's lives and to warn against lawlessness. Sincerely, In view of this, we are sending a letter to your office as representatives to clarify the facts and request a fair investigation to protect the people's lives. Sincerely, To the Chief of the Police Department of the Public Works Department,"

Further Investigation of the Morphine Factory Case on Rue Foochow 163

The three-story Western-style house at No. 12, Alley 456, Rue Foochow was the location of a large-scale morphine manufacturing operation organized by Ningbo native Zhang Zheng-gao and others. Around 3:00 AM the previous morning, Chinese detectives Wang Runhe and Wang Guangqi of the Hongkou police raided the premises and arrested Jiang Jin-dao from Tongzhou, Tang A-jin, Zhang A-gen, Yu A-xian, the woman Chen Ji-shi, Chen Zhang-shi, all from Ningbo, and others. They also seized morphine manufacturing equipment, chemical apparatus, a large quantity of drugs, raw materials, white powder drugs, heroin, two ledgers, and a truck and taxi used for transportation, taking everything to the police station where the suspects were detained separately. This was previously reported. The next morning, they were sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. The police lawyer Wang Yaotang presented the case and requested an extension. A portion of the evidence was presented. When questioned, Jiang Jin-dao claimed that a small bag of morphine found on him was purchased by a friend, Wang A-san, because his wife suffered from stomach problems, and he had nothing to do with the operation. He asked for leniency. Tang A-jin confessed to working there for about three weeks, earning twelve yuan per month. The boss was Zhang Zheng-gao, Zhang A-gen was a young assistant, Chen Zhang-shi was his sister, and Chen Ji-shi was a servant. An engineer named Sun Yuan produced over ten liang of morphine every night. Zhang Zheng-gao lived at No. 15, Baolin Lane, Avenue Edward VII, and he frequently came to oversee everything. He did not know the other shareholders. Chen Ji-shi admitted to being a maid, earning five yuan per month, only cooking and doing laundry, and knowing nothing else. Zhang A-gen confessed that Zheng-gao was his father, and he wrote the two ledgers presented as evidence. The court asked him to write a few key words to verify his handwriting. Chen Zhang-shi said that she had come to Shanghai from Ningbo and was temporarily staying at her mother's house at No. 15, Baolin Lane, and knew nothing else. Yu A-xian said that he lived at No. 1, Tongfu Road and was not a shareholder in the operation, and his answers were evasive. Judge Xiao Xie-fen ordered them to be remanded in custody for further investigation and verification at a later date.

Fraudulent Cotton Yarn Firm

Police Request a Postponement of the Investigation 172

Shao Jintao from Changzhou recently set up a fictitious Mao Qing Cotton Yarn Firm at No. 9, Weishui Lane, Zilai Street in the French Concession. He hired his fellow townsman Huang Yongxiang as an accountant to collude in fraudulent activities, successively defrauding large sums of money. Da Xin Guo Cloth Shop at No. 11, Qianji Lane, Tianjin Road, ordered cotton yarn from the firm and paid with two Chunyuan Zhuang bills totaling 1,212 yuan. Heji Cloth Factory at No. 6, Yongqing Lane, Laozha, purchased cotton yarn and paid with a Shanghai Bank check for 366 yuan and 5 jiao. Hui Xing Thread Factory at No. 2, Lane 433, North Shanxi Road, purchased cotton yarn and paid with two Baofeng Zhuang bills totaling 549 yuan. Sen Tai Cotton Yarn Firm at No. 27, Xingsheng Street, purchased cotton yarn and paid with a Cui Kang Zhuang bill for 254 yuan. San Xin Dyeing Factory at No. 10, Chezhan Road, Xiaoximen, purchased goods and paid with a Guohua Bank check for 270 yuan. Fu Xin Cloth Factory at No. 4, Penglai Lane, Penglai Road, purchased cotton yarn and paid with an Yi Chang Zhuang bill for 271 yuan. A total of six households were defrauded of a total of 2,649 yuan. The delivery dates were all scheduled between the 17th and 18th of the month. When the delivery dates arrived, the firm was unable to fulfill the orders, and the people had disappeared without a trace. After the victims learned of the situation, they reported it to the police. Detective Bao arrested the accountant Huang Yongxiang at Shao's residence at No. 13, Xinmin Village, Malang Road, and brought the red sandalwood furniture purchased by Shao, worth two or three hundred yuan, to the police station. They were sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the Second Special District Court for investigation. The police lawyer Chen Ming first presented the case, stating that the police had not yet investigated the case and requested a postponement to investigate and prosecute. When questioned, Huang Yongxiang stated that all the bills were collected by Shao alone, and as the accountant, he was unaware of the details and had no collusion. Judge Qiu Huan Ying reviewed the statements and ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody for further questioning at a later date.

Wei Ya Old Restaurant Expands 173

The Wei Ya Restaurant, the main branch on North Sichuan Road near Wuchang Road, is a famous Cantonese restaurant in Shanghai. The restaurant is known for its exquisite cooking, delicious flavors, and attentive service, which has made it popular with customers. Business has been booming, and the restaurant has often been full. The restaurant has recently expanded its floor space, modernized its rooms to cater to the tastes of modern customers, and ensured that all seats are spacious. It has a grand Zhongshan Hall that can accommodate more than twenty tables for banquets and celebrations.

Shanghai Bicycle Manufacturing and Sales Association Holds a General Meeting 174

Re-electing the Executive Committee

The Shanghai Bicycle Manufacturing and Sales Association, established two years ago, convened a general meeting of its members yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM to re-elect the executive committee. Twenty-two member representatives attended the meeting. Representatives from the Municipal Party Committee, Li Weixiong, the Social Affairs Bureau, Xie Jinan, and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Li Ruzhang, were present to provide guidance. Tu Runcai was elected as the chairman and Wang Disheng as the secretary. After conducting the formalities, the chairman reported on the purpose of the meeting, the association's activities, and the financial accounts. Representatives from higher authorities delivered speeches, and the following matters were discussed: ㈠ Wang Yilian, representative of the Wu Chang Bicycle Shop, a member, was a member of the first executive committee. According to reports, he had sold his bicycle shop but had not withdrawn from the association according to the regulations. His qualifications as a member representative had been lost, and his position on the executive committee should be cancelled. ㈡ Article 13 of the association's constitution was amended to add two supervisory committee members. ㈢ Promoting national goods and making efforts to sell them were unanimously approved. Subsequently, the executive committee was re-elected. In addition to Wang Yilian, who was automatically removed, two members were to be drawn by lot. The Social Affairs Bureau representative verified the drawing, and Chen Zhigen and Xu Wenyuan were drawn. Tu Runlin, Zhu Tongsheng, Qian Chuyu, and Xi Hongde retained their positions. As a result of the re-election, Yu Kun, Hu Weiyuan, and Cao Cangzhou were elected to the executive committee, and Jiang Shusheng, Sun Bingquan, and Zhu Lintang were elected as alternate executive committee members. The executive committee then mutually elected Tu Runcai, Zhu Tongsheng, and Hu Weiyuan as standing committee members, with Tu Runcai as chairman.

City Voices 177

▲Iron-Skinned Unusual Orange Arrives in Shanghai: The olives produced by Kang Le Yuan in Tai Po, Hong Kong, are crisp, sweet, fragrant, and rich, and those who taste them say they are exquisite. The garden covers hundreds of acres, but the output is extremely small. Several thousand pounds were previously available, but they sold out in a few days. A large quantity of iron-skinned unusual oranges, which have never been seen in Shanghai before, has now arrived from the garden. To allow the people of Shanghai to try them at a special price, they are priced at two catties per yuan, with a limit of one yuan per person. There are also more than one hundred pieces of local Chinese sweet oranges and more than one hundred barrels of white olives, which have also arrived in Shanghai at the same time. They are distributed by Xing Hua Lou on the Four Horses Road, and Yuan De and Heng Yu grocery stores on Guangdong Street are also selling them.

▲Tang Xie Cheng Wine Shop Offers Special Prices for the Spring Festival: Tang Xie Cheng Wine Shop on Minhang Road, Xiaodongmen, has been in business for twenty years. It has always adhered to the principles of "truth" and "sincerity," never deceiving customers with inferior goods or attracting customers with price reductions. It is particularly careful in selecting goods and treats customers with courtesy and harmony, so it has been praised by all walks of life. As the Spring Festival is approaching, the owner is hospitable and offers special prices on all kinds of wine to thank the public for their appreciation. Both retail and wholesale are welcome.

In addition to scout supplies, it also has a daily necessities department, a sports equipment department, and an educational supplies department. National goods factories that wish to contact for consignment sales or manage their products are welcome. It is said that the official opening will be on February 5, and there will be a grand occasion with many visitors.

▲Star Floral Dew Perfume Special Sacrifice Sale: The Sino-Western Pharmacy on Four Horses Road is offering special low prices this time, purely in the spirit of sacrifice. In addition to world-famous tonics, which are sold for only one jiao per bottle, it will also reduce the price of the trial bottle of Star Floral Dew Perfume, which can also treat frostbite, to five fen from today onwards. The pharmacy also has a kind of hemostatic medicated cotton wool, a must-have for families. For knife wounds and burns, a small amount of this cotton wool can stop bleeding and close the wound. Each package is reduced to one jiao and five fen.

Calligraphy and Painting News 178

▲Zhang Dan'an Donates a Thousand Books: Zhang Dan'an, a calligrapher from Biling, has many students all over the world. His true script, running script, official script, and seal script each have their own characteristics. He has retired to Shanghai and enjoys calligraphy every day. However, Mr. Zhang is eccentric by nature and never shows his work to others easily. Last year, his close friend Mr. Wu, at the request of a book collector from Japan, offered a thousand taels of silver as a gift to ask for a piece of calligraphy, but Mr. Zhang refused. His high moral character can be seen from this. Recently, due to the repeated requests of relatives and friends, he reluctantly broke the rule and donated a thousand pieces of calligraphy to broaden his circle of friends. Anyone who presents today's newspaper issue to Mr. Zhang to request calligraphy within five feet will be charged a ink fee of one yuan, and a matching couplet with the inscription will be added. This offer is limited to one thousand pieces, and no more will be accepted beyond that. Four screen strips will cost two yuan. Paper will be provided. Mr. Zhang is not using this to make a profit, but only to amuse himself. Those at home and abroad who wish to obtain his calligraphy should send a letter to Mr. Chen Mengdie, c/o Yadong Bank, No. 44 Tianjin Road, Shanghai, or No. 58 Changsheng Street, Nine Acres, with the ink fee enclosed. The reply will be sent within five days.

Reading Q&A

Reading Plan (3) 180

Reading Guidance:

I am very fond of history, especially Chinese history, but because I cannot enter university at present, I plan to study on my own in my spare time. I have written my "Self-Study Plan" below and respectfully request your guidance.

After graduating from middle school, I went to work in society and have been doing so for five years. When I first graduated, I did not like any of the subjects very much, because at that time I only liked to play! After I started working, things gradually changed. The whip of life was constantly lashing me, causing me to live in a state of boredom and pain all day long. So I became fond of studying, in order to make myself feel better mentally. Because I like to get to the bottom of everything, I wanted to study history. This is why I chose history as my subject of study.

I have now read several general national histories, such as the high school national history textbooks of major bookstores and Wang Tongling's "General History of China," but after reading these books, I still cannot get any benefit, because they do not tell me the overall activities and social changes of mankind, or the Chinese nation. They do not let me know the influence or causal relationship of the past on the present. They only tell me the names of some great figures and heroes, how great their abilities are, and how extraordinary their talents are, as if these people are a different kind of people, completely different from us mortals. They only tell me about the changes of dynasties, the transfer of power, such as the decline of the power of eunuchs and noble relatives. They only tell me about domestic and foreign wars, foreign invasions, and so on. As for why this is so, and what the situation was at the time, they never give me any hints.

Later, I also read some history about cultural relics and systems, but it was also chaotic and unsystematic. In short, these books are all condensed versions of large historical materials, not "history."

Now I can no longer rely on these history outlines and other books. I want to study directly from historical materials.

I originally planned to study from ancient times all the way down, but the text of ancient Chinese books is very difficult to understand. Even after reading the annotations, I am still at a loss. Therefore, I feel that in order to study Chinese history, one must first be proficient in philology. So my first step now is to prepare to study "textual studies" and archaeological studies. I plan to do this research for a year.

After I have a rough understanding of these, I will read ancient books, and read Chinese history books one by one in a systematic way (the books I plan to read are detailed in the bibliography).

Although the plan has been set, I have the following questions: First, there is not enough time for research. It is really difficult to study Chinese studies. At first, I thought that textual studies could be mastered soon, but after buying a "Textual Studies" book and reading it, I felt that this thing was not easy either, and it could not be mastered and applied without a long period of study. Then, thinking about the twenty-four histories, which are so many books, I don't know how much time it will take to finish reading them. How can someone like me, who has so little time to read (at most three hours of free time every night), finish reading them? Second, reading textual studies and ancient history (such as "Zizhi Tongjian") is too boring to arouse my interest. Third, the books are insufficient and not enough for research.

With the above points, I have doubts about my reading plan, fearing that it cannot be realized, so I hope your department can solve my difficulties. Or help me make a self-study plan, but I hope you pay attention to my purpose: I do not want to be a historical expert, I only want to understand the past situation of the current society, so that I can understand why the current society is like this.

--Letter from Huang Xiuzhong--

Spring and Autumn

Standards for Marrying a Wife 184

— Qi Ling

Which man does not marry a wife? Unless he is an unsound cripple. But no one has the leisure to examine what kind of woman is a standard wife? Therefore, many results are unsatisfactory, and their focus is not obtaining a standard wife.

Therefore, I feel that this issue is worth discussing, especially for young people who are about to get married or have lovers. It is even more urgent to study whether the other party meets the conditions of a standard wife before uniting. Otherwise, it is truly so-called [misleading for life], which can cause considerable harm.

Based on my personal observations, a standard wife must have the following six conditions:

(1) Good Moral Character: As the saying goes, [marrying a wife is about marrying virtue]. If you marry a woman who is a [Hedor Lion's Roar] or [frivolous and unchaste], then what family happiness is there!

(2) Sound Physique: [A sound mother can give birth to a sound child]. What I am saying here is not about being as robust as an athlete, just not being [weak and sickly].

(3) Proper Appearance: A beautiful wife can cause trouble, which has been true since ancient times. Therefore, I think an ordinary-looking wife is also acceptable, as long as she doesn't have pockmarks or scars, cross-eyes, or a crooked mouth.

(4) Does Not Love Being Modern: At most, three parts modern, and must be seven parts old-fashioned. Because the so-called modern decoration costs are not enough for us poor guys to buy a pair of high heels with a month's salary.

(5) Proficient in Writing: Can women with extensive knowledge of Chinese and Western studies really apply what they have learned? Furthermore, it is not that I look down on women's rights, but if you teach your wife to go out to earn money to support the family or support her husband, China has not yet reached this level. So, a basic understanding of writing is enough.

(6) Able to Assist with Household Affairs: The first purpose of marrying a wife is to [continue the family line], and the second purpose is to assist with household affairs. Because the husband is away all day, if the wife is also away all day, or stands by idly, without paying attention to any household affairs, then what can she be called a [good wife]? The above six points are just my personal observations.

Wife 185

— Lonely Xu Sheng

A fortune teller said: [Wife, wealth, children, and status]. It can be seen that these four things are the treasures that people care about the most; otherwise, why wouldn't the fortune teller use other treasures to cater to people's psychology? I might as well talk about the first treasure: the wife.

Who doesn't have a wife? Who doesn't want to marry a wife? Of course, a wife is an important fellow. Therefore, apart from new people calling their wives [My Love], when ordinary people are in their honeymoon period, who doesn't call them [Baby]? Of course, a wife is a source of comfort in spirit and body, providing warmth and care, sharing the bed, giving birth to sons and daughters—all of which are the wife's due obligations; therefore, ancient people called them [Inner Helper]. Liang Hong and Meng Guang personally wielded the pestle and mortar; Sima Xiangru and Zhuo Wenjun sold wine at the stove; Jing Zhao painted eyebrows, and the romantic stories were passed down; historically, they are all said to be virtuous couples. Even the great American novelist Washington Irving, in his essay "A History of New York," wrote: [It is only in times of distress that a man knows the virtues of his wife]. [When in despair, getting pillow talk, solving my worries; looking around when going out, relatives and old friends, none of them being affectionate, all acting disdainfully; only at home, affection is still the same, still with the air of being uniquely respected, and the spirit is boosted]. Irving was an old man, and he still said such things, which shows that people in China and abroad all regard their wives as treasures.

A wife is indeed a treasure because [wife education] is more practical than any other education. What about mother's education, father's education, brother's education, teacher's education? They can't compare; therefore, [being afraid of one's wife] is an element of a person's success. As the saying goes, [Being afraid of one's wife leads to wealth]. That is the reason. Who doesn't want to get rich, so many people are afraid of their wives. The current widespread wife education is nothing more than [getting rich] and [becoming an official]; perhaps those who get rich and become officials benefit from [wife education]. However, the wife education of the ancients was different from that of today. In the Song Dynasty, there was a man named Yang Pu, and Emperor Zhenzong summoned him to write poetry; he said he couldn't. Zhenzong asked him, "Did anyone write a poem to send you off when you left?" Yang Pu said, "No, only my old wife wrote one, saying: [Rest from your poverty and drunken revelry! Stop your reckless love of poetry! Today, you are being dragged into officialdom; this time, you'll lose your old head]". Zhenzong laughed loudly and let him go without making him an official. The mentality of wives today is completely different from that of the ancients; therefore, husbands rack their brains, desperately making money and scheming in every way, wanting to win a smile from their wives.

Wife 186

— Ding Hua

[Lock the door when you go out, no fire when you come into the room, no one to make worn-out shoes, no one to mend torn socks, you know the suffering of being without a wife when you have one.] The above is a love song of unmarried people, and my second uncle seemed to sing it when he hadn't married four years ago. Indeed, when a person reaches a certain age, marriage is also a very necessary thing. Besides making shoes and socks for you, the benefits that a wife can give you are that she can comfort you when you are frustrated, and she can help you when you are not capable of doing something.

But marrying a wife is not an easy thing. You have to consider the other person's appearance and pay attention to their inner self. Even if you marry a lover who you like and who likes you, there are still problems. Strindberg's [Love and Bread] describes a clerk in the Council Office who earns two hundred and fifty kronor a month, named Fack, who did not carefully consider the bread problem after marriage and the problem of raising children in advance, and went to marry his lover, Louise. In the end, it turned into a tragedy, and the result was that his wife and son were taken away by his father-in-law, and the creditors took everything from his house: chairs, shelves, mahogany beds, knives, forks, pots, plates, basins, kettles…

The above story shows the reasons for the endless stream of divorce cases in China today!

The Ideal Wife 187

— Rui Qing

She grew up in a poetic ancient city; she is the daughter of a scholar, so she has received a good education.

She is the gentlest, most beautiful, most sincere, most affectionate, and noblest; a person who is sound in both body and mind.

Her gentleness is neither mediocre nor foolish, nor is it cowardly; she is like a cool breeze after the scorching heat of summer, gently caressing people, making them feel refreshed and comfortable all over.

Her beauty is not decoration, not clothing; she has a shapely figure, a pretty face, rosy skin, elastic muscles, and a smart and lively spirit, so people feel that she is beautiful in every way.

Her sincerity is not hypocrisy, not entanglement; she has no selfish views, she can love and care for her husband meticulously; regardless of joy, anger, sorrow, or happiness, everything is a pure expression of her heart.

Her affection is permanent and unchanging; her nobility is natural and subjective.

Her body is extremely beautiful and healthy; neither fat nor thin, moderate in length. She can exercise, dance, swim, and…

Her knowledge is very accurate: she can write, compose, paint, play music, sing, socialize, sew, cook, raise children, and manage the household… In society, she is a social butterfly; at home, she is a virtuous housewife.

She has grown up in my heart since childhood, and her virtues, talents, and everything else have gradually grown day by day. I cannot forget her for a single day, hour, minute, or second.

But where is she now?

Friends who are dreaming of the joy of getting married! Before you prepare to marry a wife, don't forget to measure yourself. Do you have the ability to solve the bread problem after marriage and the problem of raising children? Otherwise, you will only be acting out a tragedy that Fack and Louise acted out. As for the practical benefits of a wife, you won't get any, so why bother?!

Husband and Wife 188

— Bing Hua

That Saturday, I went to Takabashi to play, and when I got home, it was past dinnertime. As soon as I entered the door, my wife's face showed displeasure and she said:

[You must have had fun today].

[Not really...] I answered vaguely, because I knew my wife was angry.

[I thought you wouldn't be back so late, I was afraid your soul had been taken away].

[You always like to say too much, please forgive me this time, I'll come back earlier next time]. I said to my wife in a pleading tone.

[Come back or don't come back, I won't care about you anymore, please find someone else to take care of the household chores]. My wife was still furious.

So the quarrel began.

After three minutes of silence, we were both angry and silent. I smoked a cigarette, and I felt even more annoyed. I ran upstairs to sleep, and although my eyes were closed, I didn't fall asleep.

Not long after, my wife came up too. She saw that I was sleeping with my clothes on, and seemed to feel sorry for my tiredness. She gently took off my leather shoes, took a quilt, and covered me, and put down the curtains. At that time, I pretended to wake up and saw that the anger on my wife's face had long disappeared. I felt relieved.

[Are you still angry with me? Beat me up to vent your anger, okay?] I leaned my head on my wife's body in a coquettish way. [Who is angry with you?... I love you even more now, you know?] My wife said from the bottom of her heart.

I looked at the clock on the table and it was already ten o'clock.

[I forgot to eat dinner]. We both said in unison.

[The food at home is cold. How about we go out to eat? And then go to Vienna to dance?]

[Whatever...] my wife said, and gave me a sweet, long kiss.

[Oh! You didn't shave your face today, it hurts my face].

My wife said with a smile.

[...]. I also smiled.

In this smile of looking at each other, our husband and wife were still as good as ever.

(Response)

Talking About Being Afraid of One's Wife 189

— Le Ye

The debate between male-centered and female-centered has not yet been resolved, and it is not an easy thing to solve. Proponents of women's rights say that Chinese women have been groaning under the oppression of men for thousands of years, and now they want to stand up and liberate themselves. This is not wrong. Indeed, Chinese women have suffered thousands of years of pain under the constraints of ritual education, but men who oppose women's rights say that although Chinese women are constrained by ritual education, this is in name only, but in fact, women's rights are higher than everything. This is not wrong either. [Being afraid of one's husband] is not often heard, but [being afraid of one's wife] is a household name, very common, and has existed since ancient times.

[Being afraid of one's wife] is a very common thing. Now, due to changes in the times, the way [being afraid of one's wife] and [controlling one's husband] has also changed. In the past, most women had bound feet and did not leave the house all year round. Even when they went out, they sat in sedan chairs, with maids and servants protecting them, walking a few streets. How would they know about things outside? Therefore, old-fashioned women controlled their husbands only at home and set a time limit for returning home at night. If there was a violation, they would wait to exercise their power—a queen's command, but the execution of that command could only be limited to within the queen's chamber. It could not extend beyond the chamber. Unless they received a secret report, a man's misdeeds outside could definitely not be controlled by a virago. Now the times are different, and women's great power in foreign affairs has surpassed that of men. Places where men go, such as dancing, swimming, drama, and other entertainment venues, also cannot be without women's footprints. Not only do men become women's advanced followers. During a man's routine work, if he wants to kill time, his wife usually has the right to accompany him, or even has the possibility of forcing her husband to engage in a certain kind of entertainment. Therefore, many men, wanting to engage in irregular entertainment, are unable to do so because of surveillance.

Therefore, now women are constantly monitoring their husbands' actions. As for the men's side, wanting to engage in some improper entertainment, in the past they were afraid of their wives knowing! Now they are afraid of their wives seeing, and the fear is the same, but the method is a bit different.

Life Imprisonment 190

— MO

Quite by chance, I encountered my old classmate Mr. H, whom I hadn't seen in ten years, on [Mystery Street], which gave me unexpected joy. According to custom, old friends meeting again cannot avoid borrowing cups and plates to tell each other what they have been doing since we last saw each other. I couldn't avoid this custom either, so we went together to the Xin Ya Tea House, which we used to frequent.

We sat down in a quiet corner. We ordered two cups of tea, a few appetizers, and a catty of aged Hua Diao wine. The waiter brought the wine and dishes. We poured wine and chatted casually. We talked about the country's precarious situation, and we also talked about the mother school's precarious state; finally, we talked about the issue of spouses.

[Have you gotten married?] Mr. H asked me.

[I'm ashamed to say! I'm thirty years old, and my wife's position is still vacant.] I answered coyly].

[You are so happy!] Mr. H said with an envious tone. [Happy? I see that the classmates and friends I know all have young, beautiful, and modern wives. In the bright mornings and moonlit evenings, under the shade of trees, in theaters, they live sweet lives together. Some even have a crystallization of love, a lovely little baby, to add to the family's liveliness. And me, besides half a box of luggage and two shelves of old books, what's left is just a stark bachelor. Whenever the night is waning and people are quiet, whenever it's a cold rainy night, how lonely I feel in life, how desolate I feel as a bachelor! Your life, old friend, is truly happy and makes me envious!] After I finished speaking, I took a deep sip of Hua Diao wine, watching Mr. H, waiting for his opinion. Mr. H said with a very sad attitude: [Old friend, you're so smart, how can you only see the joy of marriage? As the saying goes: [Marriage is the tomb of love]! I can now add a transitional phrase: [Marrying a wife is the pronouncement of a fixed-term imprisonment!] Since we parted from school, I was very lucky to find a job that couldn't be considered small in K Province, and the income was not small, so the problem of livelihood was solved, and I went to look for my future beautiful wife.

[Soon], Mr. H took a puff of smoke and continued: [A new acquaintance in K Province introduced me to a certain lady who graduated from a local girls' school. Ms. Someone, my current wife, at that time, was indeed young and beautiful, and her knowledge and talent were not bad. So, I, who had been craving a woman for a long time, accelerated from acquaintance to friend to lover to marriage. And the execution of my fixed-term imprisonment also began at that time.

[Before I got married, my life was so comfortable, my actions were so free. Once I got married, it was as if a person engaged in political activities had encountered a secret agent, and I was being monitored by my wife everywhere. This can also be forgiven. What's most unbearable is that the numbers in my bookkeeping also underwent drastic changes. At first, it changed from surplus to break-even, and later it turned into a deficit. According to my wife's academic ability, under these circumstances, she could have gone out and done some kind of job to make up for my shortcomings. However, labor should only be done by the husband. Her job every day is just to think about how to dress up, how to make new clothes, how to boast to the same sex, and how to please the opposite sex. I, for the sake of women, can only endure like a dumb person eating huanglian.

[Two years later, that son, who was praised as the crystallization of love, was born. That's right, sons are something that adorn the shortcomings of a family in other people's homes. But for me, it's like a prisoner who has served his term and is released from prison committing a crime again, and therefore sentenced to life imprisonment. What hiring a nanny, holding a full moon ceremony, and all the burdens, put pressure on my upright body and turned me into a hunchback. [Now, my dog is already of school age. If I don't let him go to school, I'll be failing in my responsibility as a father; but if I let him go to school, under the modern commercialized school system, you can't go to school without money. Because of all this, I have long wanted to escape from prison. But you, my old friend, are craving the taste of sugar-coated poison, how unwise!]

After Mr. H finished speaking, those worldly eyes stared at me terribly, waiting for my ideal rebuttal. I could only be like under the guidance of a dignified parent, just saying Yes and OK.

CUHK Dean of Academic Affairs

Sun Benwen Resigns: The Process 191

Sun Benwen, the Dean of Academic Affairs at Central University, has also been a professor in the Department of Sociology at CUHK for many years. He is determined to study academics and lacks interest in administrative affairs. When Luo Jialun took over as the president of CUHK two years ago, he asked Sun to concurrently serve as the Dean of Academic Affairs. At that time, CUHK was in the aftermath of the turmoil. For the sake of the school's future and feeling Luo's sincere entrustment, Sun agreed to serve concurrently temporarily. In the year or so, the school has been rectified and stabilized, so he repeatedly resigned from the concurrent position of Dean of Academic Affairs to Luo, specializing in teaching in the Department of Sociology, so as to concentrate on academic research. Because Sun's intention to resign was very firm, Luo had no choice but to approve his resignation from the concurrent position, and hired Chen Jianxiao, a professor of educational psychology, to succeed as the Dean of Academic Affairs. In addition, Huang Jianzhong, the dean of the College of Education, was also repeatedly urged by Luo when he took over, before he agreed to temporarily serve as the dean concurrently. At the end of each semester, he firmly resigned from the authorities. At the end of this semester, Luo was unable to retain him any longer, so he asked him to specialize in teaching as a professor in the Department of Education and the Department of Philosophy, so that he could concentrate on academic research, in line with his personal interests. It is heard that Ai Wei has been asked to succeed as the dean of the College of Education. Ai has been a professor in the Department of Psychology at the school since Dongda. Last year, he was sent to the UK by the Cultural Foundation Board of Directors for investigation and has only recently returned to China.

Ministry of Interior Consults Ministry of Education

Emphasis on Cultivating Water Conservancy Talents 192

Instructing domestic engineering colleges to expand water conservancy engineering courses

And establishing departments of water conservancy engineering in relevant engineering colleges

丨丨Proposal from the North China Water Conservancy Commission丨丨

The Ministry of Education issued a circular to the education departments and bureaus of all provinces and cities, stating: "Regarding the approval of the Ministry of Interior's letter No. 22 regarding land matters, it states, 'This Ministry has convened the Second National Internal Affairs Conference, and all resolutions adopted have been reported or circulated separately. Now, the North China Water Conservancy Commission has proposed that the conference recommend that the Ministries of Interior and Education emphasize the cultivation of water conservancy talents and establish a hydraulic engineering museum. This has been recorded in the minutes of the conference and sent to the Ministry of Interior for handling. The success of any undertaking depends on the planning and execution of specialized talents, and the training of talents should be based on the needs of society. Water conservancy is related to the national economy and the people's livelihood, and there are many urgent matters to be addressed. The original proposal suggests expanding courses related to water conservancy engineering in domestic engineering colleges and establishing departments of water conservancy engineering as appropriate to train technical personnel to undertake this arduous task, which is indeed an urgent priority. Furthermore, water conservancy is closely related to the interests of the people, and it is essential to impart basic knowledge. The original proposal to establish a hydraulic engineering museum is also an important plan. However, the equipment is complex and difficult to implement. The Ministry suggests collecting and displaying models, photos, and atlases of hydraulic engineering in museums or exhibition halls related to public education, which would be easier to implement and have the same effect. Regarding the above two items, we request that your Ministry review them and instruct relevant departments to implement them earnestly to promote education and water conservancy. The original proposal is enclosed for your review and handling. Thank you.' A copy of the original proposal has been sent to the Ministry. It is imperative to cultivate water conservancy talents and display models, photos, and atlases of hydraulic engineering. In addition to issuing separate orders and replies, a copy of the original proposal is enclosed to instruct the relevant departments to refer to the local situation and needs and handle it accordingly. This order, with the attached proposal (omitted)."

Xu Beihong's Painting Exhibition in Berlin: A Great Success 193

▲Positive reviews from German newspapers

(Berlin Correspondence) Painter Xu Beihong brought more than forty of his works to Berlin. Introduced by the President of the Berlin National Academy of Fine Arts, the greatest contemporary German painter, he was able to hold a public exhibition in the "Berlin Artists' Association". The exhibition started in mid-November and lasted for several weeks. People in Berlin paid close attention to it.

The art world was particularly excited, and many reviews were published in major newspapers. The Berliner Tageblatt, the most widely circulated newspaper in Berlin, devoted half a page in its illustrated supplement on November 28 to reproduce five of Mr. Xu's animal paintings (Jiu Fang Gao, Lazy Cat, Amazement, Chicken, and Poetic Interpretation of the Six Dynasties). It also published a lengthy critique entitled "Animals from China", praising Mr. Xu's vivid and powerful depiction of animals, which were proud and unconventional. Two excerpts are translated below: "[...] Yes, it is precisely this pride that distinguishes them from ordinary beasts. They possess a unique life sentiment. The horse led to Jiu Fang Gao stands tall and proud, its eyes and nostrils expressing its life force, even more so than the posture of its body. And the eyes of this horse connoisseur, while sharply scrutinizing, are also full of the same noble and proud expression. He is full of passionate greatness." "[The animals in the paintings jump and run, as if they are all preparing for a new action. It is usually difficult to paint animals because it is hard to express their agility in such a lighthearted way. It is even harder to make them have flesh and blood with ink and oil paint, but it has been successfully achieved here."

Current Situation of Education in Anhui Province (I) 194

丨Observation Report by Special Commissioner Li Ximou of the Ministry of Education丨

The observation report on education in Anhui Province by Li Ximou, Special Commissioner of the Ministry of Education, is nearing completion. The original text is very long, and excerpts are recorded below.

㈠ Current Situation of Secondary Schools 195

One provincial senior high school, eight middle schools from the First to the Eighth, six girls' middle schools, one girls' normal school, one girls' secondary vocational school, nine secondary vocational schools from the First to the Ninth, three rural normal schools, one joint Anqing Six Counties Middle School, one Ning District junior middle school, Tongcheng County Middle School and county junior middle schools in various counties, and Xuan Cheng County Girls Junior Middle School, totaling twenty-four schools, four county secondary vocational schools, four private middle schools, fifteen junior middle schools, one girls' middle school, two girls' junior middle schools, one Wuhu Vocational School. There are a total of eighty-one secondary schools for both boys and girls in the province, with twenty-eight provincial schools, thirty joint and county schools, and twenty-three private schools.

㈡ Current Situation of Education Funding and Independent Plan 196

Before the twelfth year of the Republic (1923), education funding in Anhui Province was uniformly allocated directly to schools by the province based on the approved budget. However, due to frequent shortfalls in fiscal revenue, arrears accumulated over the years, especially for administrative and other expenses. After several twists and turns, the province followed the independent model of Jiangsu and designated cigarette taxes as special funds. At that time, as it was a new initiative, the tax revenue was minimal. It was not until after the sixteenth year of the Republic (1927), when tax rates were increased, that education funding gradually stabilized. Coincidentally, the central government reorganized finances and divided national and local taxes, and the cigarette tax was reformed into a unified tax, resulting in the loss of supplementary education funding. Later, due to the efforts of people throughout the province, the finance and education departments went to Beijing to negotiate, and the central government agreed to subsidize 100,000 yuan per month, totaling 1.2 million yuan per year. Currently, most of the annual education funding in the province relies on this subsidy. The remainder is allocated by the finance department from provincial funds according to the approved budget. The allocation of provincial education funds for the twenty-second year of the Republic (1933) is as follows: 158,180 yuan for education administration expenses (plus 9,000 yuan for temporary expenses), 572,333 yuan for higher education expenses (plus 36,000 yuan for temporary expenses), 1,325,509 yuan for secondary education expenses, 335,580 yuan for primary education expenses, 100,944 yuan for social education expenses, and 78,790 yuan for various education undertakings expenses (plus 10,200 yuan for temporary expenses). Regarding the procedures for claiming and disbursing funds, when the cigarette tax was designated as special funds in the sixteenth year of the Republic (1927), the Jiangsu province's independent model was followed, and a Education Funding Management Office was established by the finance and education departments as the education funding management agency. The collection, disbursement, and auditing of tax revenues were all managed by this office. Since the cigarette tax was taken over by the central government, the source of education funding has been divided into provincial funds and central government subsidies. The responsibilities of the office have also changed accordingly. The monthly management and disbursement procedures are summarized below for provincial education agencies, except for universities, which are handled directly by the provincial treasury: A. The central government subsidy is claimed directly from the Ministry of Finance by the management office on a monthly basis. The education department then distributes the funds according to the monthly budget of each agency and issues a list to the management office for disbursement. B. Provincial funds are claimed from the finance department by the management office. The education department then distributes the funds according to the amount of funds received each time and issues a list to the management office for disbursement. (The province also has review procedures for the reimbursement of expenses and the organization of the auditing committee, which are omitted here.) The history of the independent education funding movement in the province is as follows: At the provincial education administration conference held in the eleventh year of the Republic (1922), there was a proposal to unify education funding. In April of the same year, a Special Education Funds Management Committee was organized, designating 440,000 yuan from the land tax of Tongcheng and other ten counties, 600,000 yuan from the salt river and other customs duties, and a total of 1.53 million yuan from the tea customs duties as education funding. Later, the financial authorities advocated the unification of the treasury, overturning the previous plan. In July of the twelfth year of the Republic (1923), due to the efforts of people in the province, the provincial government designated the cigarette tax as special education funds. In April of the sixteenth year of the Republic (1927), the provincial political affairs committee established the Education Funding Management Office as the special management agency for these funds. In February of the seventeenth year of the Republic (1928), the Ministry of Finance reformed the cigarette tax into a unified tax and subsidized 100,000 yuan per month from the central government to compensate for it. As for the independent education funding plan, according to the opinions of the provincial education administration authorities, there is no other way except to raise additional salt tax. The salt in Anhui Province is divided into three regions: the central part of Anhui sells Huai salt, with an annual volume of 800,000 packages. Previously, an additional three yuan was added to each package, generating an annual revenue of over 2 million yuan, which has now been taken back by the Ministry of Finance. The southern part of Anhui sells Zhejiang salt, and the northern part of Anhui sells Ji salt, and there is no such additional tax. The education authorities of the province believe that if the example of central Anhui could be followed and additional taxes could be added uniformly to be used as special education funds for the province, not only would the tax source be stable and the revenue reliable, but the quantity would also be greatly beneficial to future development.

㈢ New Allocation of Provincial Schools from the Twenty-Second Year of the Republic (1933) 197

The current secondary education funding in Anhui Province, as listed in the budget for the twenty-second year of the Republic (1933), is 1,325,500 yuan. Among them, funding for ordinary middle schools accounts for slightly more than 39 percent, funding for normal schools accounts for slightly more than 30 percent, and funding for vocational schools accounts for slightly less than 30 percent. In order to meet the standards for the allocation of secondary education stipulated by the Ministry, one side intends to gradually increase funding, and the other side intends to increase or decrease or change the number and nature of schools. The provincial middle schools and normal schools are planned to be reorganized and divided into six normal school districts. ㈠ The names of all schools should be prefixed with the words "Provincial". ㈡ Each normal school district, except for the first district, which has separate normal schools for boys and girls, will have one normal school, all with separate departments for boys and girls, with classes taught separately. The fifth and sixth districts will also have one simple rural normal school each. ㈢ Each normal school district, except for the first district, which has separate senior and junior high schools, will have one middle school combining senior and junior high schools. The fourth district will also have one junior high school. ㈣ The original four normal schools, twelve middle schools combining senior and junior high schools, one senior high school, and two junior high schools, totaling nineteen schools, will be reorganized into seven normal schools, two simple rural normal schools, eight middle schools combining senior and junior high schools, one senior high school, and four junior high schools, totaling twenty-two schools. According to the latest planned distribution of secondary schools, ordinary senior high schools will have one senior high school in the provincial capital, Huizhou Middle School and the senior high school ordinary classes of Wuhu Middle School in southern Anhui, Fengyang Middle School and the senior high school ordinary classes of Yingzhou Middle School in northern Anhui, and the senior high school classes of Luzhou Middle School in central Anhui. There will be three girls' senior high school classes, one in Anqing, one in Wuhu, and one in Fengyang, distributed in southern, central, and northern Anhui, which seems appropriate. As for how to reorganize vocational schools and vocational departments in the future, so as to take both the principles stipulated by the Ministry and the needs of the local area into consideration, there is no different plan. However, according to the division of the province's administrative regions, there have been proposed vocational departments suitable for each region, such as agriculture (rice, wheat, cotton, flowers, vegetables, agricultural tools, miscellaneous grains, horticulture, landscaping), animal husbandry (cattle, bees, poultry), forestry, sericulture, tobacco, civil engineering, etc.

㈣ New Allocation Plan for Middle School Funding Starting from the Twenty-Second Year of the Republic (1933) 198

Judging from the total amount of secondary education funding in Anhui Province in the twenty-second year of the Republic (1933), the percentage of its allocation, except for the funding for vocational schools, which does not meet the standards stipulated by the Ministry, is generally in line with the standards set by the Ministry of Education. According to the Measures for the Establishment and Funding Allocation Standards for Secondary Schools in Various Provinces and Cities stipulated by the Ministry of Education, starting from the twenty-third year of the Republic (1934), the newly added funding for secondary education in various provinces and cities should be used primarily for vocational and normal school funding. Those who are unable to increase it should gradually reduce the corresponding amount of middle school funding from the original funding to expand vocational education and normal education. It is found that the funding for normal schools in Anhui Province has already exceeded the standards stipulated by the Ministry. If the total amount cannot be increased, there will be no need to expand in the future. Currently, the most important expansion is vocational education funding. However, according to the current financial situation of Anhui Province, it is difficult to greatly increase education funding. If it is entirely dependent on newly added funding, it is doubtful whether the standards stipulated by the Ministry can be reached in six years. However, since the middle school funding in the province in the twenty-second year of the Republic (1933) is only equivalent to the standards stipulated by the Ministry, it is also unreasonable to gradually reduce it for the expansion of vocational education. Therefore, the province has no other way to expand vocational education funding except to transfer it from the education funding itself. It is found that the province has accumulated more than 40,000 yuan in education funding for studying abroad over the years. If the number of self-funded students in Europe and the United States is reduced starting from the twenty-third year of the Republic (1934), it is estimated that the current standards stipulated by the Ministry can be reached by the twenty-sixth year of the Republic (1937).

The Education Department of Jiangsu Province Instructs All Middle Schools

Five Matters That Accountants Should Implement 199

The Education Department of Jiangsu Province instructs all middle schools: "It is found that the system of accountants appointed by the Department has been implemented since the beginning of this academic year. Currently, in the initial stages, many have not been able to thoroughly implement the measures stipulated by the Department. Now, the first semester is about to end. The Department hopes that the principals and accountants of all schools will earnestly implement the following items: 1. The accountant is appointed by the Education Department to oversee the accounting affairs of the school and practice sites. Except for consulting with the principal on handling matters, they are not subject to interference from other staff members within the school to maintain the spirit of accounting independence. 2. The principal and the accountant shall jointly bear full responsibility for the economic affairs of the school and practice sites. All expenses of the school and practice sites shall not be disbursed unless approved by the principal and the accountant in advance. Receipts for all collections should be jointly stamped by the principal and the accountant. 3. When the administrative office of the school or practice workshop pre-claims funds from the accountant for miscellaneous expenses, each time shall not exceed one hundred yuan. A second pre-claim shall not be made until the funds pre-claimed the first time have been settled. Moreover, uses of five yuan or more, or those outside the budget scope, shall still be subject to approval by the principal and the accountant before disbursement. Otherwise, the accountant may deduct the expense. 4. Income funds from practice sites shall be turned over to the accountant at any time for registration and safekeeping, and shall not be retained by the site for other purposes. The accountant shall also conduct thorough audits at any time. If it is discovered that collections are not turned over in a timely manner, it shall be considered as concealment by the handler, and the principal shall be immediately informed for disciplinary action. If the circumstances are more serious, the Department shall be directly notified for handling. 5. The principal shall fully assist the accountant in exercising their functions within the prescribed scope. They should especially strive to eliminate obstacles and assist in the progress of reforming past accounting practices. If the above items cannot be earnestly implemented by each school, the principal shall be deemed negligent and the accountant shall be deemed to have failed in their duties, and they shall bear corresponding responsibility. The Department will conduct inspections at any time and will not tolerate any pretense. In addition to distributing separately, this order is hereby issued to the principal of the school for compliance. This order."

This City

Chen Guofu and Others Initiate the Organization of the Chinese Cultural Advancement Association 200

▲Creating a Frontline for Cultural Revolution

▲Founders' Meeting Scheduled to be Held in Shanghai

Chen Guofu, Ye Chucang, Wu Tiecheng, Chen Lifu, Wu Xingya, Pan Gongzhan, and others, deeply aware that the pro-construction culture and the Proletarian culture are sufficient to undermine the Three Principles of the People's political and economic revolution, have initiated the organization of the Chinese Cultural Advancement Association to create a frontline for cultural revolution. A founders' meeting is scheduled to be held in Shanghai. The origins of its establishment, its organizational purpose, and the names of the founders are recorded below.

▲Origins of Establishment　As the times evolve, the relationship between culture and politics and economy becomes increasingly inseparable. Politics and economy are the driving forces of culture, and culture is the nurturer of politics and economy. Moreover, in another sense, politics and economy have the power to promote culture, while culture can determine the form of future politics and economy. Often, culture leads by tens or hundreds of years before the form of politics and economy is completed. Or a culture arises in one place, while the politics and economy of another place is also subject to its influence. For example, Rousseau's theory of natural human rights and Marx's theory of capital both shine in different times and countries, which is the most obvious example. Therefore, the influence of a superior culture is greater than the power of political and economic conquest. For example, the emerging Soviet Russia, Fascist Italy, and even countries like Germany and Turkey are all engaged in cultural innovation at the same time as they transform their political and economic forms, which is based on this understanding. Our Mr. Sun Yat-sen also vigorously advocated cultural revolution at the same time as he worked hard for political and economic revolution, in order to enable the culture of the Three Principles of the People to promote each other with the politics and economy of the Three Principles of the People, and to complete the highest stage of revolution in which politics, economy, and culture are united. However, since the Kuomintang came to power in recent years, it has paid too much attention to politics and economy and neglected culture, so that the transformation of politics and economy cannot correspond to the transformation of culture. The feudal culture has stood firm and defended its solid fortress, while the Proletarian culture that usurps its place has taken the opportunity to invade, forming a situation of the guest dominating the host. However, without cultural revolution, how can we promote the success of political and economic revolution? Without a united front of cultural activists, how can we cope with cultural struggles? We are deeply aware that feudal culture and Proletarian culture are sufficient to undermine the Three Principles of the People's political and economic revolution, and we have the ambition to form a revolutionary cultural frontline. Therefore, we must take it upon ourselves to organize a cultural frontline of the Three Principles of the People. This is the reason for the initiation of the Chinese Cultural Advancement Association.

▲Organizational Purpose　㈠ This Association takes creating a cultural revolution frontline as its sole mission. Anyone who has the ambition of cultural revolution, whether an organization or an individual, can become a member of this Association. However, organizations are limited to those involved in education, publishing, news, film, drama, singing, dancing, painting, and illustration. ㈡ Before the government applies totalitarianism to cultural undertakings, this Association will infiltrate the meaning of self-regulation by organizations into its organization to achieve the purpose of organizing a cultural frontline. ㈢ This Association will establish various cultural undertakings to expand the purpose of cultural movements, such as establishing schools, newspapers, bookstores, theaters, and publishing regular and irregular publications. ㈣ This Association will establish various social and mutual aid organizations to enable groups or individuals joining the Association to maintain close contact and cooperation to achieve its purpose. Although the above is only a summary, the aim of our people is already clearly visible. We now offer twelve points of enthusiasm and hope that organizations and individuals engaged in cultural movements will actively participate and jointly accomplish the great task of cultural revolution. ▲Names of Founders　Chen Guofu, Ye Chucang, Wu Tiecheng, Chen Lifu, Wu Xingya, Pan Gongzhan, Zhang Daofan, Yu Jingtang, Cheng Tianfang, Yu Hongjun, Huang Boqiao, Ye Xiufeng, Cheng Zhongxing, Xu Shaodi, Song Diao, Wu Kaixian, Bai Chuan, Tong Hangbai, Ding Mocun, Li Zhaoli, Huang Xiong, Xuan Yi, Jiang Jianbai, Pan Gongbi, Zhu Xinong, He Xiya, Dong Xian Guang, Huang Tianpeng, Ma Chonggan, Fang Huanru, Qian Cangshuo, Xue Guangqian, Hu Pu'an, Tang Huimin, Chen Baohua, Tang Zeng, Zheng Zhengqiu Shao Zuiweng, Xu Shidan, Xu Xingchu, Xu Zexiang and more than one hundred people.

New History Society of America

Essay Contest for Asian Youth 201

▲Promoting International Mutual Assistance and Understanding of National Aspirations

The New History Society of America, in order to promote international mutual assistance and understanding of national aspirations, holds an essay contest for youth around the world once a year. The first essay contest was limited to students from universities in the United States, with the topic being "How can universities promote world peace?" A total of 156 universities participated, and more than 270 essays were received. Awards were given at the International Club in New York in May 1932. The second essay contest was limited to students from universities in Europe, with the topic being "How can university youth contribute to the realization of a world federation?" Two hundred universities from 26 European countries participated, and more than 400 essays were received. Awards were given in Paris in July 1933. The third essay contest was for South America, Central America, Mexico, and the West Indies, with the topic being "How can university youth contribute to the construction of a world republic?" The results will be announced in Washington, D.C. in May 1934. Recently, the association prepared for the fourth essay contest, which began in June of this year and is limited to youth from universities in Asia, with the topic being "How can youth contribute to the realization of a global religion?" The first prize is 300 yuan, the second prize is 200 yuan, and the third prize is 100 yuan. Anyone under the age of 30, regardless of gender, can participate. The essay is limited to 2,000 words. All universities in this city have received the essay contest letters.

Lu Huipu, Secretary of the Education Department of Guangdong Province, Inspects Vocational Education in Shanghai 202

Mr. Lu Huipu, Secretary of the Education Department of Guangdong Province and Dean of the College of Engineering of Xiangqin University, after traveling north to inspect engineering and vocational education in Jiangsu and Zhejiang and arriving in Shanghai, has paid close attention to the engineering education in various universities in this city, the equipment and management of large factories in various places, and the content and promotion of industry in this city. After staying in Shanghai for about four or five days, he will travel to Wuxi and Nanjing for on-site inspections and is scheduled to return to Guangdong on February 6.

The Ministry of Education Rectifies University Education 203

▲Instructing Universities to Discontinue Unnecessary Departments

(Shen Shi News Agency, Local Dispatch) The Ministry of Education, in view of the fact that there are many universities in the country that are run seriously and meet the Ministry's regulations, but there are also not a few that are mediocre and lack proper equipment, has been actively rectifying them in recent years. It has recently sent personnel to conduct on-site investigations to ensure that they meet the Ministry's regulations and increase educational effectiveness. There has been significant success. It is now reported that a certain school still has a certain department that is not run completely, and the current situation in the country does not need this type of talent. Based on the inspector's report, the Ministry has decided to instruct several schools to temporarily suspend the department. It is reported that the circular has already been issued, but the schools that have received this instruction have not yet made any statement.

The current semester concluded the other day. The next semester will begin on the 17th of this month, and applications for transfer students in elementary and secondary schools will be accepted. A large number of free student slots are also designated, and it is reported that registration is very active.

▲Ziqiang Elementary School: Ziqiang Elementary School, located at the intersection of Gordon Road and Robison Road in western Shanghai, has been established for five years. It has recently been reported that student enrollment has increased significantly, and the original school buildings are no longer sufficient. In recent days, the registration of new students has been very active, and the admission procedures are still being handled at the original school building. You You Football Team Defeats British Navy Amidst Howling Winds 207

丨Result: 2-1丨

Slippery field diminishes performance

Yesterday, amidst howling winds and biting cold, the You You Football Team defeated the British Navy 2-1 at the China Baseball Field. This was a scene from the Western Union First Division League. The Navy's skills were mediocre and not worth mentioning. If the field had not been so slippery, diminishing the performance, the score difference would not have been so narrow. In the first half, You You played with great vigor, scoring two goals in a row. In the second half, the Navy rallied and scored one goal, resulting in a final score of 2-1. The performance of both teams is as follows:

Iron Leg Scores 208

After the two teams took their positions and the silver whistle blew, the You You forwards immediately adopted an aggressive offensive strategy. Staces made three crucial saves on the center-back line. The two Navy fullbacks, Aas and Edwards, under heavy pressure, still mustered their remaining strength to resist the You You attack, slightly diminishing its momentum. Han and Herbert found openings and frequently probed the You You defense. Jiang Shanqing stood firm, displaying a fierce demeanor. Chen Jiaqiu secretly provided support, and Nansen, receiving his assistance, penetrated the heavily guarded area and delivered a beautiful cross. Sun "Iron Leg" arrived at just the right moment and kicked the ball into the net, bringing smiles to the faces of three hundred fans.

Copper Head Breaks Through 209

Immediately after the kickoff, the Navy launched a fierce attack. Walker broke through the crowd and shot diagonally at the goal. Tang Yongchun reacted quickly, diving to block the shot and avert the danger. Huang Ruihua received the ball and passed it to Chen Huitang. Edwards failed to intercept effectively, resulting in a corner kick. Yongsen delivered the corner kick, and Edwards, attempting to clear the ball, inadvertently sent it forward. Liang Shutang intercepted it from the side and passed it to Sun Huipai, who demonstrated his 400-meter sprint speed, quickly breaking into the opponent's defensive line and crossing the ball to the center. Zhong Yongsen rushed to the scene, leaped into the air, and headed the ball into the net, leaving the Navy trailing 2-0 at halftime.

Situation Becomes Quiet 210

After the lemon break, the Navy showed renewed energy, and the offensive and defensive balance began to improve. Staces remained active, closely guarding Sun "Iron Leg" with great composure. As a result, the You You forwards appeared disorganized. Chen Huitang seemed immature, missing two excellent opportunities. The Navy forwards lacked coordination and relied solely on individual bravery, falling short of success. As time passed, the situation became quiet, with nothing particularly exciting to report. Xi Zhong and others seemed content to relax and be lazy, as if victory was already assured and no extra effort was needed.

Goal Falls 211

After a long period of chaotic play without any highlights, Staces repeatedly encouraged his teammates in the middle. Bye and Zhong Yongsen made simultaneous moves, while Edwards circled around to provide flanking support. The ball entered the center and was obtained by Robertson, who ran towards the You You penalty area. Liang Shutang turned to intercept, but Robertson passed to Walker, who passed it back into the center. Han Herbert advanced a few steps and powerfully kicked the ball. Tang Yongchun reached out to block, barely touching the ball, but it still went into the net. Afterwards, You You launched two fierce attacks on the opponent's defense, but they were unable to score. The game ended with a score of 2-1.
