A Major Case in the Sports World

The Marriage Scandal of Lu Ming, National Games Shot Put Champion 214

Abandoning His Wife and Children

Engaged to Ms. Liu Jinggui

Suddenly Married Ms. Teng Shuang

According to the Peiping Jingbao on the 19th of this month, Lu Ming, the shot put champion of last year's National Games, represented our country at the Far Eastern Games when he was at Nankai Middle School in Tianjin. Later, he transferred to Shanghai Jiaotong University, and his reputation has not diminished. He has been to the Far East four times and is now thirty-four years old. After returning from the National Games in Nanjing, he married Ms. Teng Shuang, a female athlete from Peiping, just two weeks later. Currently, Lu Ming is still employed at the Xiahuayuan Station of the Ping-Sui Railway Bureau. Yesterday, Ms. Liu Jinggui sent a letter from Xuanhua to Peiping, recounting the details of her engagement to Lu Ming in Xuanhua and stating that she will file a lawsuit. The original letter is disclosed below for the public to judge: Fellow countrymen, please be aware of this inhuman person. Most people who pay attention to sports news know him. He is Lu Ming, the shot put champion of last year's National Games. Ugh, thankfully he is just a shot put champion. If his status were any higher, who knows what kind of evil he would commit. This Lu Ming was originally a

Country Bumpkin. His parents, hoping for their son's success, used the money they earned from hard labor to support his education. Who knew that once he entered the city, he would have strange ideas and try to be modern because he had a small reputation in the sports world. Alas, [modernity, modernity, how many sins in the world are born from this!] The first problem on his mind was that his old wife was not fashionable enough, and he wanted to have a romance. He went home and disregarded his parents' heartache and his wife's old love, driving his wife and children out of the house. The woman's family was ordinary and dared not speak out, and they settled for some alimony. This is the trend of the times, and divorce is free, so this is not much. Immediately after the divorce was the

Pursuit of a Target. He ran into snags everywhere. Because these things would damage the reputation of you gentlemen, I won't go into detail. Finally, he met Ms. Teng in Zhangjiakou. This woman, with discerning eyes, actually fell in love with him. We can imagine how flattered he was. But not long after, he was about to change his mind about Ms. Teng, so he ran to Xuanhua and asked his friends to introduce him to women. He earnestly told others that "women from other places are simply unreliable and no longer talk about love." Then he told everything about Ms. Teng in detail. His friends, listening to his

Sweet Talk, thought he was sincere and had no other intentions, so they tried to help him. One of them, who had once taught me, introduced me to him. I have never been one for socializing and knew nothing about Lu Ming's history. But I trusted my teacher completely and without error, so I consulted my uncle and a cousin (who were both Lu Ming's friends). As a result, everyone agreed, and with the parents arranging the marriage, I got engaged to him. It was a surprise when I found out about his marriage to Ms. Teng in the newspaper on November 1st of last year. When I got this news, I began to suspect Lu Ming's character. On the one hand, he

Was Engaged to Me, and on the other hand, he married someone else. He married someone else, so I was mystified by his trick of bullying the weak. Soon he came to me and said, "My marriage to Ms. Teng was forced and not my intention at all," so he still asked me to fulfill the marriage contract. But later I learned that Ms. Teng had agreed to bear a portion of his ex-wife's alimony. Ah, I understood. He wanted to marry two women at the same time, but could I agree to such a request? He cried and begged me, but I refused him several times. Seeing that this trick didn't work, he asked others to mediate to

Cancel the Engagement, but I didn't allow it. How could I tolerate such a social parasite and beast in human clothing? I have my own way. Well, this is how he, the "shot put champion," sold his love and personality, and the person he deceived was a student of his friend. I can't help but recall Chairman Lin's advice to athletes to pay attention to morality. Liu Jinggui tearfully reports.

Zhejiang Education Department Orders Distribution of Physical Skills Test Form for Middle School Students 226

The Zhejiang Education Department believes that the purpose of physical education in schools is to enable young men and women to have the necessary health, physique, and resistance, and to promote the development of their physical functions. Secondary schools are an important stage in education, and their main purpose is to cultivate healthy citizens. Therefore, physical training is a crucial plan. The department has printed and distributed a Physical Skills Test Report Form for students in secondary schools and above throughout Zhejiang Province, ordering all schools above the secondary level throughout the province to conduct accurate tests on all students and submit the completed forms to the department by the end of March of the 23rd year, as a basis for setting standards for assessing physical education performance. In addition to the school grade, student gender, age, height, and weight, the form includes 28 items for physical skills. Fourteen instructions are attached to the form.

Economic Special Issue　　Published every Monday　　Issue 58

The Evolution of Land Ownership in China 229

— Chen Honggen

Our country has long emphasized agriculture, a practice unmatched or predating other nations. Eight or nine out of ten common people are engaged in farming, a tradition that has endured for thousands of years, highlighting the importance of agriculture in our nation. In the past, with a sparse population and limited foreign trade, good governance could guide the people to self-sufficiency. However, since modern times, we have suffered from foreign invasions, internal strife, natural disasters, and oppressive governance. Furthermore, the stagnation of agricultural practices has hindered innovation, leading to the collapse of the self-sufficient rural economy. Those who speak of reform advocate for political reform or the development of industry and commerce. Despite the clamor of opinions, little progress has been made. Although human failings may be a factor, the error lies in the focus. Agriculture is the foundation of the nation. Today's social problems, while increasingly complex due to industrial and commercial development, are intertwined with agricultural issues, and the agricultural problem centers around the tenant farming system. Why? Since the abolition of the well-field system in the Qin dynasty, a private tenant system emerged. [Land is not owned by the tiller; some have land but do not till... One person owns the land, while ten till it. Thus, landowners accumulate wealth and become powerful daily, while tillers subsist on meager portions and become impoverished and destitute.] (Su He). This is why society is in constant turmoil without a day of stability. Therefore, the extent of land concentration must be investigated. This article aims to outline the distribution of land ownership and the reasons for its variations.

(1) The Current State of Land Ownership Distribution in China

The distribution of land ownership refers to the allocation of land rights among farmers. According to the Ministry of Agriculture and Commerce's statistics from 1919 (tables omitted), the total number of farm households in the country was 29,548,529, of which self-cultivating farmers accounted for 58.7%, tenant farmers 22.9%, and semi-self-cultivating farmers 18.4%. The highest tenant farmer rates were in Fujian and Zhejiang, reaching 34.3%, Anhui 32.3%, and Jiangsu 30.3%. The lowest rate was in Chahar at 9.6%. Other provinces, such as Shaanxi, Shanxi, and Suiyuan, also had very low rates. Professor Buck of our school conducted a survey of land ownership among 2,866 farm households in seventeen locations across seven provinces in 1921. In North China's Hebei, Henan, Shanxi, and northern Anhui provinces, self-cultivating farmers averaged 76.5%, semi-self-cultivating farmers 13.4%, and tenant farmers 10.1%. The highest tenant farmer rate was only in Wutai, Shanxi, reaching 60.2%, followed by Su County in Anhui at 20%. The remaining areas were all below 5%, while Yanshan in Hebei and Kaifeng in Henan had no tenant farmers. In contrast, the average for self-cultivating farmers in central and eastern Anhui, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Fujian was 48.2%, semi-self-cultivating farmers 21.3%, and tenant farmers 30.5%. In Zhenhai, Zhejiang, the tenant farmer rate was as high as 76.1%, Lai'an in Anhui 50.5%, and Jiangning Taipingmen in Jiangsu 48.4%. The remaining areas, such as Wuhu, Lianjiang, and Wujin, were all around 13%. In total, the tenant farmer rate in the south was more than three times higher than in the north. Furthermore, according to statistics from the Ministry of Industry, the distribution of land rights is as follows:

North China　　　Manchuria　　　Central China　　　South China

Self-cultivating farmers　65.4　　　47.3　　　40.40　　　33.8

Tenant farmers　18.0　　　28　　　35.39

In 1927, Tan Pingshan also published a study on the proportion of agricultural population classes, and his conclusions were generally similar to the previous ones. There are also several sources of data for surveys of provinces, cities, and counties, which may be more accurate.

Jiangsu Province | According to the Jiangsu Agricultural Survey Records (published for the Jinling, Suchang, Shanghai, Hai, Huaiyang four circuits), landlords account for 37.3%, semi-landlords 27.6%, and tenant farmers 36.1%. The tenant farmer percentage recorded in the Industrial Journal is smaller, at 29%. Qiao Qiming also investigated the situation in Kunshan, Nantong, and Su County. Tenant farmers account for 77.6% in Kunshan, but only 25.5% in Su County.

Zhejiang Province | According to a survey of 85 villages in 20 counties in western Zhejiang, self-cultivating households account for 32.9%, tenant farmer households 36.7%, and semi-self-cultivating households 30.4%. The tenant farmer rate is slightly higher than in Jiangsu, which is consistent with the statistics from the Ministry of Agriculture and Commerce.

Yangqu County, Shanxi Province | A survey of twenty rural villages in Yangqu County by the Shanxi Rural Education Improvement Society found that self-cultivating farmers accounted for 60% to 80% of the population in most areas, with Yulinping reaching 93.5%. The highest tenant farmer rate was in Heitugang at 30.3%, and the lowest was less than 1%, proving that many people own land and farm it themselves.

Yunnan and Guizhou | Due to the sparse population, the tenant farmer rate is lower than in the southeast. According to the Economic Survey Report of the Hunan-Yunnan Railway Yunnan-Guizhou Section by the Ministry of Railways in 1932, there were a total of 463,750 farm households in the section, with self-cultivating farmers accounting for 40%, semi-self-cultivating farmers 30%, and tenant farmers 20%.

Overall, these statistics indicate that the distribution of tenant farmer percentages in our country is not consistent. It varies from province to province, county to county, North China differs from South China, and the Northeast is different from within the passes. Zhang Xinyi has made the following comparison: |

Northeast Region　　Yellow River Basin　　Yangtze River Basin

and its Northern Region　　and its Southern Region

Self-cultivating farmers　　51%　　　69　　　32

Semi-self-cultivating farmers　19　　　18　　CardArray

Tenant farmers　　　30　　　13　　　40

In short, the tenant farmer rate is highest in the southeast, lowest in the Yellow River Basin, and intermediate in the Northeast.

(2) Reasons for Differences in Tenant Farmer Rates in Different Regions

(1) Economic Reasons:

(A) Level of Land Price | The higher the land price, the lower the ability of poor farmers to purchase land, and the land falls into the hands of the rich, and the number of tenant farmers increases. According to statistics from the National Government's Directorate-General of Budget, Accounting and Statistics, the country is divided into seven regions, with the two provinces in the Southeast region having the highest land prices. The highest price for paddy fields in Guangdong reaches 250.5 yuan per mu, and Fujian is also as high as 200 yuan. Next is the Southwest region, with Sichuan paddy fields at 225 yuan per mu, Guizhou 200 yuan, and Yunnan 140 yuan. In Jiangsu and Zhejiang, it is 140 to 150 yuan per mu. Among the Yellow River Basin, the highest is Shandong at 170 yuan, Hebei 150 yuan, and Shaanxi is generally worth about 30 yuan per mu. In the Northeast provinces, only Liaoning is relatively high, with high-quality paddy fields around 100 yuan per mu, while ordinary fields in Heilongjiang and Jilin are only about 10 yuan per mu, with some as low as less than 1 yuan. The price of dry land is also high in the Southeast region, which is why its tenant farmer rate is higher.

(B) Degree of Industrial and Commercial Development | In regions with developed industry and commerce, the demand for agricultural products is high, and farmers often engage in intensive farming to increase their production. However, this type of farming requires sufficient capital. Farmers generally have weak financial resources, and if they purchase land, there will be little left, and working capital (for purchasing fertilizer, farm tools, wages, etc.) will be lacking, resulting in reduced harvests. It is more beneficial to rent land from others and use one's own capital for operating expenses. The coastal areas of southeastern China have highly developed industry and commerce, far surpassing the provinces of North China and the Northeast, so it is reasonable that their tenant farmer rate is higher. The surge in tenant farmers after the Industrial Revolution in England was also due to this.

(C) Relationship to New Lands | Agriculture in our country began in the Henan area. Hong Mai's Rongzhai Essays [In the era of the Zhou dynasty, the land of China was the narrowest... Among them, China was only Jin, Wei, Qi, Lu, Song, and Zheng]. Later, as the population gradually increased, it expanded to the south, seizing land and turning it into virgin land for landlords to invest and develop. Initially, it evolved into a feudal system, which later transformed into a private tenant system. Therefore, the number of tenant farmers in the south increased day by day. Although the northeastern provinces are also virgin land, due to the difficulty of transportation and the severe climate, they are not suitable for planting. The Qing dynasty also prohibited immigration to the Northeast, so the percentage of tenant farmers is not as high as in the south.

(2) Natural Reasons:

(A) Soil Quality | Southern China is suitable for growing rice, and three harvests can be obtained in a year. Northern China is suitable for growing wheat, and the conditions are inferior to those in the south. Moreover, rice eaters account for two-thirds of the country's population, so the demand is high, the price is high, and the profits are also high. Landlords tend to go to the rice-growing areas in the south to get higher rents.

(B) Climate |:

(甲) Temperature | Most of China has a continental climate, especially the northern and northwestern provinces. Temperature changes often tend to be extreme. The temperature in northern January is often below freezing, and the summer is hot. It is not inferior to the south, which hinders the growth of agricultural products. In the Yangtze River and coastal areas, the warm wind arrives from time to time, and Guangdong is like spring all year round, which is very suitable for the development of crops. (乙) Rainfall | There is very little rainfall in the north, and the distribution is not timely. According to the German Hann Gulins Von, the average annual rainfall in the north is about 21 hours, 70% of which falls in June, July, and August, which does not help the growth of crops. The rainfall in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Fujian, and Guangdong is sufficient, and the distribution is timely, so landlords tend to gather here.

(C) Disasters | Disasters of floods and droughts are often seen in our country, and their regions are mostly in the north. Floods are mostly caused by the overflow of the Yellow River, and droughts are due to insufficient rainfall. According to the British Consul in China, A. Hosie, between 620 and 1619, China experienced 442 droughts in the north, 352 in the central region, and 252 in the south. The great drought in Shandong in the fifteenth year of the Guangxu reign was particularly rare. In the fifteenth year of the Republic of China, a major drought occurred in the Northwest again. From the perspective of floods, in the past thousand years, there has been a flood in the Yellow River Basin almost every ten years. In the south, from the Tang and Song dynasties to the Qing dynasty, there were only 17 floods in Zhejiang during the Southern Song dynasty. Landlords are also unwilling to invest in disaster-prone areas to reduce their income. (3) Social Reasons

(A) Population Size | In densely populated areas, land is not sufficient for distribution, and the tenant farmer rate will inevitably increase. At present, Sichuan, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Guangdong, and Fujian provinces have the highest population densities, each with about 30 million people, while Shanxi and Shaanxi provinces have only about 10 million people. Considering the population density statistics from the Legislative Yuan, Jiangsu has 813 people per square mile, Zhejiang 554, Shanxi 183, Shaanxi 164, and Chahar 12. This is enough to show the reason for the difference in the tenant farmer percentage.

(B) Level of Living Standards | Southern farmers have a better standard of living than northern farmers, and the expenses used for necessities such as food are also greater. According to Buck's survey, the annual consumption of each farm household in North China is 190.36 yuan, while in Central and Eastern China it is 288.63 yuan. If the spending in the south is extravagant and the income is abundant, it can still be maintained. However, in the event of a famine, it is difficult to maintain life, or borrow money to build up debts, so they have to sell their land and become tenant farmers. Twelve, seventeen, Yu Jindai

Roosevelt's Silver Policy and China (Continued) 230

— Wei Qi

2. The Need for Silver

Generally speaking, the need for silver can be divided into three categories: currency use, arts and crafts and industrial use, and storage by Indians and Chinese. Everyone knows that silver is used for art, decorations, and silverware, so there's no need to elaborate.

The main industrial use of silver is in the photographic industry, especially the motion picture film industry. It is said that the motion picture film industry consumes about 60 million ounces of silver per year, of which about 80% of the silver from unused film is chemically reduced. Therefore, the actual consumption is about 12 million ounces per year. The silver consumption for arts and crafts in the past ten years is as follows, most of which was used by the United States.

Silver Consumption for Arts and Crafts and Industrial Use (Unit: Million Ounces)

1921　　51　　1926　　Not Available

1922　　68　　1927　　40

1923　　61　　1928　　61

1924　　58　　1929　　58

1925　　Not Available

From this, it can be seen that the silver consumption for arts and crafts and industrial use is generally around 50 to 60 million ounces per year, without significant increases or decreases. Therefore, it is clear that this aspect cannot influence the price of silver significantly.

As currency, silver is currently used only in China and a few insignificant colonial countries. Although gold standard countries and de facto gold standard countries also use silver as subsidiary currency, they have been gradually reducing its use recently. The following table lists the annual silver coin minting volume of the two largest silver-using countries, China and India, since 1914:

From this, it can be seen that India minted 150 million ounces of silver until 1919, but after that, it decreased significantly, minting only 620,000 ounces in 1930. Although China's silver coin minting volume has not increased significantly in recent years, it accounts for more than half of the world's total minting volume. Therefore, China's economic conditions have a significant impact on the price of silver.

Indians and Chinese have a great fondness for silver, so most middle-class families use it as a means of accumulating wealth and storing it. According to Silas, at the end of March 1919, Indian civilians had 3.729 billion ounces. Since then, there have been annual imports, and now there are at least 4.2 billion ounces or more. China's silver holdings are also more than 2.5 billion ounces, of which about 150 million ounces are dead silver. The following table lists the net silver imports of India and China:

Under these circumstances of oversupply, insufficient demand, and the deepening of the world economic panic, the sharp drop in silver prices is an inevitable phenomenon and does not need to be explained in too much detail. 3. Roosevelt's Silver Policy and Its Impact

Above, we have briefly reviewed the reasons for the decline in silver prices. Now, let's look at whether Roosevelt's silver policy can raise and stabilize silver prices to increase domestic and foreign trade, and what impact it will have on China.

According to a New York dispatch from the Havas News Agency on December 22 of last year, Congressman Pittman, the proposer of the silver resolution at the World Economic Conference, expressed enthusiastic support for President Roosevelt's decision to mint silver coins. He told the press: "After the United States takes this action, major silver-producing countries such as Canada, Australia, Mexico, and Peru will follow suit and emulate the United States... Roosevelt will stabilize the world silver price to 64.5 cents per ounce, which will increase the purchasing power of the currencies of China, India, Mexico, and South American countries by 60% compared to the US dollar, and will also increase the general purchasing power of the United States by 50%, and will have the same effect as lowering the price of the US dollar." In his proclamation of minting silver coins, President Roosevelt also stated: after his own investigation, he felt that it was necessary to raise and stabilize silver prices in order to raise and stabilize domestic prices, increase the purchasing power of silver-using countries, and protect US foreign trade from the adverse effects of foreign currency depreciation. From the above two quotes, it can be seen that they believe that raising the price of silver to 64.5 cents per ounce will increase the purchasing power of the currencies of China, India, Mexico, and South American countries by 60% compared to the US dollar, to benefit US foreign trade, raise and stabilize domestic prices, and increase the general purchasing power of the United States by 50%, in order to overcome the domestic panic. However, will major silver-producing countries such as Canada, Australia, Mexico, and Peru follow suit as Pittman said, and will the price of silver be permanently stabilized at 64.5 cents per ounce? This is a question worth studying. I think it will probably be like the observation of the London financial community, which said that the US purchase of gold failed to influence world prices, so this US silver policy may have the same experience. When silver-using countries and silver-producing countries announced their silver sales agreement at the World Economic Conference, the price of silver only rose slightly, but then immediately reacted. Therefore, the future situation should be the same. It is estimated that speculators in the United States have about 150 million ounces of silver in stock that they are eager to sell. Although last year's silver production was only 160 million ounces, a decrease of 80 million ounces compared to the average of the past ten years, the world's accumulated silver is still very large. And the opinion of Wall Street in New York is that this new monetary policy may not have a significant effect on raising silver prices immediately; it is estimated that the total inventory of silver bars, excluding those held by the US government, is as high as 105 million ounces. In addition, US silver production accounts for only one-sixth of the world's silver production, and according to the London Silver Agreement, India can sell 35 million ounces of silver on the world market each year, while the total amount of silver held by Indian private individuals is about 75 million ounces, which is not restricted by the agreement. In total, India holds 422.788 million ounces of silver (according to Silas's calculation we cited above, the actual amount is more than this). At the end of 1931, Shanghai's silver reserves reached 190.934 million ounces. Although the London Silver Agreement stipulates that China cannot melt down silver coins, silver ingots widely used in China, with a price of one to five taels, are not subject to restrictions. In recent months, due to expectations that silver prices would rise, as many as 30 million ounces of these silver ingots have been shipped to the United States for sale. From this point of view, the tendency of the US silver price to rise may be stalled by the large-scale influx of foreign silver and the recent intense speculation in silver in the United States. From this, it can be seen that the US government wants to maintain a relatively long-term stable silver price of 64.5 cents unless it prohibits the import of foreign silver. But this would inevitably lose its global effectiveness and would not help in practice. Therefore, to permanently restore silver prices, only a unified restoration of bimetallism by all major countries in the world, and overcoming the current world economic panic, and increasing the use of solutions, can achieve the goal. History has already told us that artificially suppressing or raising prices is only a temporary stimulant and will never be long-lasting.

The London Silver Agreement, which has been approved by India and the United States, seems to have established its foundation. Even if all signatory countries can fully approve and implement it before April 1 of this year, and raise silver prices, that will only be for a period of four years. After four years, once this chain is broken, a large amount of silver will flow out of the national treasuries of various countries into the market, which will undoubtedly create a lower price than the current one.

However, even if we leave aside the matter of four years later for now, and only talk about Roosevelt's silver policy and the London Silver Agreement, assuming that they can raise silver prices, what impact will that have on China? First, we can see that after the price of silver rises, China will inevitably suffer more from the invasion of imported goods from gold standard countries, and at the same time, it will inevitably lead to a sharp decrease in China's exports. Under this situation of a large trade deficit, China, lacking gold to pay for the settlement difference, will inevitably have to export a large amount of silver; as a result, the circulation of domestic banks and paper money in China will inevitably contract, leading to the bankruptcy of banks and stores, and accelerating the rapid collapse of China's rural economy. Secondly, we can see that China's silver reserves will flow out in large quantities due to the stimulation of rising silver prices overseas, causing panic in China's finances. In addition, the government's fiscal revenue will inevitably decrease sharply and be on the verge of crisis due to the reduction in the amount of gold and silver conversion of customs revenue. From this, it can be seen that Roosevelt's silver policy and the London Silver Agreement are nothing more than a policy of US imperialism attempting to transfer the burden of panic to silver-using countries in the East, especially China. Therefore, in the current situation of world economic panic, widespread price declines, and consistent implementation of currency inflation in various countries, we would rather have silver prices fall than artificially raise silver prices like Roosevelt and the London Silver Agreement.

Outline for Reorganizing Land Tax in Jiangsu Province 231

This publication's 48th issue has already mentioned the main points of how Jiangsu Province's land tax should be reorganized. According to reports, the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance has established a complete and comprehensive plan for the land tax reorganization work in various counties, which will be implemented step by step by county. The plan it has set can be compared with the previous article in this publication, so it is recorded below. It should also be noted by those who are concerned about Jiangsu's finances.

(1) Investigation and Compilation of Land Tax Registers: The biggest cause of the land tax problem is the lack of land tax maps and registers, and the lack of a basis for collecting land tax. Since the loss of the Fish Scale Registers, the collection officials in various counties have no actual collection registers to rely on for each household, and can only rely on the existing books to collect from each household, relying on the clerks. The root cause of all the malpractices in the land tax lies in this. Therefore, the first problem to be solved is how to obtain complete land tax maps and registers, and how to obtain the names of the business households in the flower household registers. Of course, the fundamental solution to this point is to implement land survey. After the land survey, complete maps and registers can be obtained, and various problems can be solved easily. However, land survey takes a long time and is very expensive, and it is definitely not something that can be done in the short term. Before the land survey is carried out, the method of investigating and compiling land tax maps and registers is to first carry out land reporting in the areas of each county where the land survey has not been carried out and the registers have been lost, or to strictly implement universal promotion and collection, which will be handled by the district, township, and town chiefs together with the bookkeepers, and the original grain registers will be collected and cross-checked with each other to compile household and lot registers as the basis for the current grain collection.

(2) Reorganization of Land Tax Surcharges: Everyone knows the complexity of land tax surcharges in Jiangsu Province. The pain that people feel from land tax is also the most severe due to surcharges. Various counties arbitrarily impose surcharges, with complex names and different purposes. Statistics show that there are as many as 105 types of surcharges in the province, and the surcharges exceed the regular tax by more than ten times. Although some of them have regular taxes that are too low, which makes the surcharges particularly high, the fact that they are complex and complicated is undeniable. People do not suffer from the regular tax, but from the surcharges. If the surcharges cannot be paid, even the regular tax cannot be paid, which has a significant impact on the province's revenue. Therefore, the most urgent thing to do in the reorganization of land tax is to reorganize the surcharges in various counties. There are about four methods for reorganizing surcharges: (1) Unify the names. The various surcharge names in various counties should be classified and merged according to their nature, and the percentage distribution ratio should be set separately. Only two names should be on the string vote: provincial tax and county tax. (2) Review the uses. A local budget review committee will be set up by the department group, and the county magistrate of each county will be convened to thoroughly review the additional uses. (3) Reduce the tax rate. This will be done at the same time as the review of uses. The surcharge rates in various counties that are too high will be strictly reduced to reduce the burden on the people. In the future, various counties will be strictly prohibited from arbitrarily increasing surcharges and taxes. The above items are already in active progress, and it is said that the reorganization will be completed in three months.

(3) Improve the Collection System: Improving the collection system and implementing strict auditing are essential for improving the land tax. If people can understand the tax payment procedures, they will not be deceived by the clerks. If the authorities can audit the collection, the clerks will not embezzle the tax funds. If the treasury system can be strictly implemented, the tax funds can be deposited into the treasury on time. It is said that the urgent things to do in reorganizing the land tax in various counties include: ordering various counties to announce the land tax laws, abolishing silver and rice, changing to collecting national currency, improving the land tax payment procedures, reforming the string vote, and strictly implementing legislation for business households to directly pay grain.

It is said that the above reorganization steps are all for the counties in the first phase of the initial reorganization period. The counties that are already surveying the land will proceed with the second phase of the reorganization measures. However, it is said that the second phase plan is closely related to the land bureau in terms of implementing land surveys, conducting registration, and estimating land prices in various counties. The Department of Finance and the Provincial Land Bureau will cooperate to take close contact steps.

Finance: Foreign Exchange Reduced to Two Points 232

Yesterday, because it was Sunday and the banks were closed, there was no delivery of money as usual. The foreign exchange market price in the market was two points in both the morning and afternoon markets, a sudden decrease of three points compared to the previous day. The reason was that the transaction of exchange bills decreased sharply, and the market was very loose. It is estimated that the turnover in the morning market was more than 3.4 million, new transactions were more than 300,000, transactions in the afternoon market were more than 400,000, transactions in the Small General Association were more than 300,000, the remittance of foreign public bills by money houses was more than 28 million, and there was no delivery of foreign exchange. The amount owed by various routes was more than 300,000. The market price of subsidiary currency: the price of Jiangnan small foreign coins was 845 yuan in both the morning and afternoon markets, a decrease of 2 yuan compared to the previous day. Transactions were made, with 5,000 jiao in the morning market and 4,000 jiao in the afternoon market. The price of Guangdong small foreign coins was 791 yuan in the morning market and 791 yuan and 6 jiao in the afternoon market. Transactions were 40,000 jiao in the morning market and 35,000 jiao in the afternoon market. The price of copper coins was reduced by 1,000 wen to 294,000. Transactions were 33,810 strings, with a total value of 11,500 yuan in foreign currency.

Securities: The Bond Market During Last Week's Storm 233

Resulting in Gains Ranging from Several Cents to $1.35

From January 15th to 20th last week, the market prices at the Chinese Securities Exchange fluctuated dramatically. Since the Fujian Incident, after the recovery of Fuzhou, it seemed things might settle down. However, the 19th Route Army, like a cornered beast, continued to fight, and the Southwest mobilized again, sending large forces into Fujian, creating the impression of "playing the lute and singing." Although the conflict between Sun and Ma was a local issue, the possibility of escalation meant the central government couldn't ignore it. The Fourth Plenary Session had already convened, but the potential for hidden reefs ahead caused concern. With only a few days left for the Exchange's January futures contracts and approximately 80 million in margin accounts, the market, after a brief period of stability, experienced significant turbulence again within a day or two. Today marks the start of the final four days of trading for this month's futures, coinciding with the Fourth Plenary Session, suggesting further volatility in price fluctuations. On Monday, with the recovery of Fuzhou, market prices rose only slightly at the opening, with only the top stocks gaining a few cents. The rest generally weakened, resulting in an overall decline of about half a yuan, due to the general belief that the final hope had been realized, leading to a rush to sell. This unexpected trend created doubt, and steadfast investors were unwilling to blindly follow, leading to a stalemate on Tuesday and Wednesday, with prices fluctuating minimally. On Thursday, the short sellers' positions showed signs of weakening, and suddenly, a large amount of funds were spent on No. 46, but the market price only increased by 3-5 cents. On Friday, despite the pressure from No. 46's selling, the eagerness to cover short positions far exceeded it, and various bonds reached new highs. Troop Reorganization Bonds broke through 66 yuan, and Salt Tax Bonds surged past the 50 yuan mark. The rapid gains resulted in a sudden increase of over one yuan throughout the day. On Saturday, a frenzy of selling from No. 4, even more intense than No. 46, made it difficult for the market to sustain gains, showing slight signs of fatigue. Over the week, although the price fluctuations were significant, they were not the most extreme, mainly due to speculation about the success of the upcoming Fourth Plenary Session, causing some turbulence. Once the resolutions are announced, there will likely be even larger waves, especially considering the final three to four days of the month. The market ultimately saw gains ranging from several cents to $1.35, with a total transaction volume of 94,639,000 yuan.

What I Hope Medical Educators Will Advocate 236

— Yu Yunxiu

(Continued from Issue 54)

㈢ Equipment Issues

When it comes to equipment, naturally, universities and specialized schools should have adequate facilities. As the old saying goes, "To do a good job, one must first sharpen one's tools." No one can oppose this principle. However, in our impoverished country, those in charge of education must lower the standard for equipment. We must understand that the purpose of our equipment is for teaching and research, so the standard of equipment should be sufficient for teaching and research. To put it extremely, for example, if one wants to culture bacteria, if the school is poor and cannot afford many good incubators, using thermos bottles as a substitute is not necessarily impossible. For example, if one wants to preserve the current state of bacteria and prevent them from developing, if the school is poor and cannot afford many good refrigerators, using a few wooden boxes filled with sawdust and wood shavings, and then adding some ice, can also serve as a substitute for a refrigerator, and it will have a considerable effect in curbing the development of bacteria. It is not necessarily impossible to succeed. This kind of "poverty-stricken" research work should have considerable value in our impoverished country. I will give it a badge and call it "austere research," which happens to imitate health work and is the opposite of the "austere hygiene" that I mentioned above. Therefore, I believe that for the equipment issue in medical schools, we should only require that it be sufficient for teaching and research. If there is no money to buy many good incubators for culturing bacteria, then thermos bottles will do. If there is no money to buy many good refrigerators for curbing bacterial growth, then wooden boxes will do. As for the instruments that are absolutely indispensable and cannot be replaced, of course, they must be prepared. If we develop our country's medical education and medical research with this kind of advocacy, this kind of mentality, and this kind of plan, then our impoverished country will have hope. If we violate this idea, forget the economic situation of the entire country, forget that we were born as ordinary people in an impoverished country, act confused and filthy, flatter and smile obsequiously, and start swaggering around as soon as we get a little money, looking down on rickshaws while riding in cars, dismissing those who ride in small carts as if they were not human, and treating charcoal braziers as worthless after using hot water heaters, then not only is one's mind, insight, and capacity not worthy of emulation, but, to put it bluntly, one does not want medical education in our impoverished country to develop. People who hold this view must either have other motives or have a slight mental disorder. If it is solely for the sake of teaching, so that students can broaden their horizons and knowledge, and avoid being treated as if they came from a small family, then there are even better ways. Just buy several sample books and explain the diagrams to the students in detail, and that will be enough. If not, take them to see and learn from different places. As for where they will work after graduation, the scope of work will definitely be limited. The instruments and techniques used in this limited scope can be learned temporarily, in a few hours at the very least, and in two or three days at the most. This is not a major obstacle to a medical career. People who will only read in a bright and clean room and only practice writing with fine pens and beautiful paper are definitely not good students. They are only cultivating extravagant habits and are prone to disappointment and discouragement when they enter impoverished society! However, although I make this argument, I still advocate that schools should do research if they have the opportunity, but they should not dismiss and reject those who cannot afford to do research. Furthermore, they should not forget to support them and help them improve.

Short Comments on Medical Affairs 237

— Pang Jingzhou

丨Jiao Yitang's Resignation丨

Last week, various newspapers published a Nanjing dispatch, which roughly stated: "On the 12th, at a meeting of the Legislative Yuan, members Jiao Yitang and Peng Yangguang, because the National Medical Center Regulations they proposed were opposed, left in anger before the meeting ended and immediately submitted their resignations." Another message said: "In the National Medical Center Regulations proposed by Jiao, the director was to be appointed by simplified procedure, and the section chiefs were to be appointed by commission, which resembled the organization of a government office. Some people opposed the establishment of another redundant agency, and Chairman Sun Ke put it to a vote. As a result, it was rejected by a vote of 42 to 10. Jiao then left the meeting hall with his briefcase and immediately drafted a letter of resignation with Peng Yangguang." Later, the newspapers reported: "After Chairman Sun's retention of Jiao and Peng, and the promise to resubmit the National Medical Center Regulations for review, the intention to resign has been withdrawn."

Based on the above facts, it is already sufficient to vividly depict Jiao Yitang's thoughts, insights, character, and learning. His act of resigning and withdrawing his resignation is just like a tantrum. Moreover, he, who also serves as the director of the National Medical Center, must obtain a simplified procedure appointment.

The Legislative Yuan is one of the five branches of the government, and one-fifth of the national affairs relies on this meeting to resolve them. It is not a place to exclusively discuss national medicine. Because one case did not meet his private intentions, Jiao left the meeting hall with his briefcase. Where does he intend to place his remaining responsibilities? Where does he intend to place national affairs? In a meeting, if the minority does not obey the majority and can arbitrarily walk out of the meeting hall, I am afraid that all the committee members of various meetings can run away completely. What else can be discussed? If the country's legislation is handed over to people like this, isn't it terrible!

The world's medicine is already tending towards unity. Should the Chinese medical community use the term "national medicine" to confront Western medicine, sensible people have already said so. Recently, Mr. Wang Jingwei's remarks were very good: "Since medicine is to be divided into national medicine and Western medicine, then should the military also be divided into the national army that uses broadswords and the Western army that uses machine guns! Therefore, there is only a distinction between scientific medicine and non-scientific medicine, and there should be no separate category of 'national medicine'!" This statement is extremely thorough and has won the sympathy of the majority of people. The rejection of the National Medical Center Regulations by the members of the Legislative Yuan this time may be due to Mr. Wang's insightful remark. That is why Jiao was so anxious.

Jiao Yitang is so loyal to the National Medical Center. In the end, I don't know what medicine he is selling in his gourd. Some people say that he has other political purposes. Some people say that he is foolishly loyal and does not understand the general trend. However, even according to the tone of his letter to the people, saying something about preserving national essence and resisting foreign goods is just as pleasant to hear as the Boxers' "Support the Qing and destroy the foreign." Unfortunately, today's national affairs must go through the system of meetings. Otherwise, Jiao could just like Duanhua and Sushun in those years, deceive the Empress Dowager Cixi alone and do a thorough job of the National Medical Center.

Jiao's tantrum has already taken effect and has already gained the face of being retained. In fact, it is not considered to be loyal to the country. It would be best to have another "corpse remonstrance" and simply leave a suicide note to the President of the Legislative Yuan and other members. It is expected that the National Medical Center Regulations will be safely implemented, and it will save the trouble of roundabout maneuvers to submit them for review. Fortunately, the Boxers wanted to kill foreigners, so the Eight-Nation Alliance came to resolve the situation, and Duan and Su were convicted. National medicine does not harm foreigners in the slightest, so of course, no foreigners will interfere. I guarantee that not only will he not be executed, but he may also receive incense and flower offerings and become a living Buddha of the people.

After Saying Goodbye to Western Suits 238

— Song Guobin

Because my giving up Western suits for Chinese attire has attracted a lot of attention, although my article "Farewell to Western Suits" was partly playful in nature, it can be said to be a kind of personal awakening and a promotion to my friends and relatives. People like Chun Yukun and Zhuang Zhou often combined satire with humor, and my article, at the very least, cannot be said to be without purpose!

It has been more than a month since I changed to Chinese attire! In this short period of time, it is certainly impossible to talk about any achievements, but I have already received its benefits in terms of hygiene! For more than ten years of wearing Western suits, I often suffered from colds every winter. Although it was not like most people's runny noses and coughs, even this minor cold always felt uncomfortable. Since abandoning Western suits and changing to Chinese attire, although the time has been very short, the problem of winter colds has also left me with Western suits. As for the warmth and comfort of the body, it really gives me a good impression! On the streets where the north wind is whistling, it does not seem to feel too uncomfortable. And the friends who generally wear tight sleeves and hard shirts and think they are beautiful, their shrinking appearance, as I see it, there is a sense of "that time is different from this time"!

My personal experience of changing to Chinese clothing is like this, as for my students? In the past, Western suits accounted for 70-80% of them. After I changed to Chinese clothing, after my repeated persuasion, most of them have already changed to Chinese clothing! They used to suffer from winter colds like me, but now? They have also said goodbye to this hateful cold like me. From a hygienic point of view, Chinese clothing cannot be said to be without any benefits!

I am ashamed to say that my two goals in saying goodbye to Western suits, namely, promoting hygiene and recovering rights, have at least achieved the first goal! The second one is difficult to say, because my personal strength and the strength of many students in my school are very small, and it seems that it will not help. This is to hope that patriotic compatriots will give it a promotion! The things in the world are related to each other, and the benefits of Chinese clothing are as described above, but is there no inconvenience? This is not the case. Chinese clothing also has its own troubles. This trouble is not the trouble of Chinese clothing itself, but the trouble caused by wearing Chinese clothing.

Chinese people have a special psychology of "fear of foreigners" and "worship of foreigners." Not only are they afraid of and worship true foreigners, but also Chinese products that imitate foreigners. For this reason, friends who wear Western suits are always more advantageous than those who wear Chinese clothing, especially when traveling. Once you arrive at the station, you can tell the difference! When I used to wear Western suits, I was never checked by the police at the station. Now that my clothes have changed, the attitude of the police at the station has also changed! Strict interrogation and meticulous inspection, as if not afraid of trouble, in fact, my clothes are not gorgeous, but they are also neat. Where do they know that they are wearing colored glasses? Therefore, I feel "that time is different from this time" again!

The psychology of the Chinese people is like this, and the psychology of the Chinese people wearing Western suits is also like this. Unfortunately, Chinese clothing cannot be blamed on it!

The Danger, Removal, and Prevention of Human Intestinal Parasites 239

(Lecture Manuscript from the Tzu Hang Midwifery School and Asia Middle School) Jiang Benyi

Intestinal parasitic diseases are caused by the parasitism of intestinal parasites. Since there are so many types of intestinal parasites, there are also so many types of intestinal parasitic diseases. Writing them out one by one would be both too troublesome and unnecessary. Therefore, only a few commonly seen intestinal parasitic diseases will be written about here; and for each disease, only a few very simple outlines will be given. Readers

Page 16

who are looking for advanced materials here will surely be disappointed. Fortunately, this is popular medical and hygiene common sense, as long as simple things can be explained, so that the general reader can gain some knowledge of human intestinal parasitic diseases.

Now, let me write down some of the most common intestinal parasitic diseases that we often see:

(A) Ascariasis

Ascariasis is very common in our China, probably accounting for 50% to 70%. To put it clearly, 50 to 70 out of 100 people have ascariasis.

Ascaris is a roundworm that lives in our small intestine. The male worm is about 250 mm long and 4 mm in diameter; the female worm is 400 mm long and 6 mm in diameter. When this worm is parasitizing, we will develop many disease symptoms. The most obvious are:

1. Pica

People with ascariasis! Especially children, often have different tastes from ordinary people, and like to eat wall soil, courtyard soil, chalk, incense sticks, and other things that ordinary people never eat.

2. Gastrointestinal Symptoms

Increased or decreased appetite, vomiting, belching, bad breath, bloating, abdominal pain, malnutrition, etc.

3. Toxic Symptoms

Toxic symptoms are most common in children. For example, suddenly developing a high fever and symptoms like meningitis, dizziness, convulsions, epilepsy, nerve pain, itchy nose, hearing and vision impairment, memory loss, etc.

4. Intestinal Perforation

If there are ulcers in the intestines, ascaris worms often perforate the intestinal wall and burrow out of it, thus becoming acute peritonitis and dying. However, this example is relatively rare.

5. Intestinal Obstruction

If a large number of ascaris worms gather in the intestine and cannot easily get out, it can often cause ascariasis obstruction and death. However, this example is also rare.

6. Other

Ascaris worms have a habit of burrowing into small holes, so sometimes they often burrow into our trachea, nasal cavity, lacrimal duct, and bile duct, causing various dangerous symptoms.

Ascariasis is one of the most common but not very dangerous intestinal parasitic diseases, but it already has such severe symptoms. Needless to say about others, is it necessary to remove human intestinal parasites? I think if you are not stupid, you will definitely say [yes]. Now let’s talk about other types of intestinal parasitic diseases.

(B) Duodenal Worm Disease

Duodenal worm is a small roundworm that lives in the duodenum. It is much smaller than ascaris worms. The female worm has a long diameter of 12 to 18 millimeters; the male worm has a long diameter of 6 to 10 millimeters. The color of the worm is either yellowish-white or reddish.

The most important symptom of duodenal worm disease is anemia. Therefore, people with duodenal worm disease, in addition to having symptoms similar to those of ascariasis, the most prominent symptom is anemia. As the disease progresses, the skin and mucous membranes gradually become pale. Due to anemia, the nails lack nutrition and become thin and easily broken. Wavy bumps appear on its surface. Heart palpitations, difficulty breathing. As the disease progresses further, there is a tendency to develop edema and bleeding. Not only that, but also various lesions occur in the nervous system. The most obvious ones are headaches, tinnitus, dizziness, insomnia, dreaminess, neurasthenia, cerebral anemia, epileptic seizures, and poor memory. In addition, development is also greatly affected. For example, if a child gets this disease, their mental development will be slow and their physical development will be poor. If a woman gets this disease, she will often experience amenorrhea and miscarriage.

(C) Enterobiasis

Pinworm is an intestinal parasite even smaller than duodenal worms. The male worm is 2 mm to 4 mm long, and the female worm is 12 mm long.

Although enterobiasis is much less dangerous than ascariasis and duodenal worm disease, it is very annoying when parasitized by it. Its most prominent symptom is anal itching, especially when falling asleep at night, because the buttocks are warm, and pinworms crawl out of the intestines to lay eggs on the skin around the anus and perineum, which not only makes the patient feel itchy and uncomfortable, but also unconsciously develops bad habits such as masturbation.

The symptoms of enterobiasis are mostly local symptoms. For example: balanitis, penile erection and semen leakage, prostatitis, vulvovaginitis, leucorrhea, chronic proctitis, etc. caused by local irritation of pinworms.

(D) Trichuriasis

Trichuriasis is also a very popular disease, probably accounting for 60% to 70%. To put it clearly, worm eggs of whipworms can be found in the feces of 60 to 70 out of 100 people.

The whipworm is just as its name suggests, like a whip. The front body is as thin as a thread, and the rear body is relatively thick, like the handle of a whip. Its long diameter is about 40 to 50 millimeters.

Trichuriasis has no inherent symptoms, but when a large number of them are parasitizing, it can often cause stubborn diarrhea, even mucoid bloody stools, thus leading to anemia, high fever, and various neurological symptoms, eventually leading to death.

If whipworms parasitize in the cecum or appendix, they often cause cecitis or appendicitis.

Common Knowledge Question and Answer on Diseases 240

— Cheng Hanzhang

(24) Pulmonary Tuberculosis (Continued)

(Q) What are the symptoms of progressive pulmonary tuberculosis?

(A) During the progressive stage, the fever continues to rise, the body weight gradually decreases, the lesions in the lungs expand, the cheeks are flushed, there is a kind of luster in the eyes, the complexion is pale, there is stinging pain in the chest, the anterior spine increases, a large amount of sputum is coughed up, and the sputum contains mucus or pus-like substances, the cough is severe, and repeated hemoptysis occurs, and cavities form in the lungs.

(Q) Are there any unique features in the patient’s appearance?

(A) Patients have a consumptive physique, the slope of the ribs is steep, the collarbone is prominent, the shoulder blades are winged, the chest wall is sunken due to lung atrophy, the spine is slightly forward-curved, and they are emaciated (because fat disappears and muscles atrophy). The range of heartbeats expands and rises.

(Q) What is the patient’s fever like?

(A) Fever is one of the most important symptoms of consumptive patients. And patients pay very much attention to fever. Generally, it is between 37 and 38 degrees Celsius, decreasing in the morning and rising about 0.5 degrees in the evening. As the disease progresses, it rises to 39 or 40 degrees in the evening. This kind of fever is called consumption fever, which hurts the body the most.

(Q) What is the reason for the fever in tuberculosis patients?

(A) It is probably due to the toxic reaction of tuberculosis bacteria.

(Q) What other important symptoms do tuberculosis patients have besides fever?

(A) There is also the symptom of night sweats after sleeping.

(Q) What is the patient’s cough like?

(A) The cough of consumptive patients is mainly dry cough and slight cough, and the cough is more severe in the morning and evening.

(Q) What is the condition of the sputum?

(A) When there are cavities in the lungs, the amount of sputum increases; the sputum coughed up is mucopurulent and not very thick. The sputum discharged from the cavities is often lumpy and contains a lot of blood.

(Q) Can people who have already suffered from consumptive disease be immune?

(A) The primary lung lesions have a greater tendency to heal; most of them stop with some traces of changes in the bronchial glands. When such a state recurs later and new lesions occur, it becomes a chronic and mild process. In short, at the time of the initial onset, the patient has gained some comparative immunity, so it can be so mild when it recurs.

(Q) What are the prevention methods for pulmonary tuberculosis?

(A) First, it is isolation: People suffering from open pulmonary tuberculosis should be isolated to avoid spreading the infection to others, because their sputum contains tuberculosis bacteria. Infants are most likely to get sick, and they are also more dangerous; therefore, strict isolation is necessary. Second, it is most important for patients not to cough in the face of people and to cover their mouths with a cloth. Third, the sputum must be spat in a sputum cup. Put a little disinfectant in it, such as carbolic acid water, Lysol water, limewater, etc. Fourth, clothes should be steam-sterilized and sun-sterilized. Fifth, houses and sick rooms should have sufficient sunlight and ventilation. Do not use brooms when sweeping to avoid dust flying around. Sixth, marriage has the risk of mutual infection between husband and wife. Pregnancy and childbirth are both dangerous, so attention should be paid to them. Seventh, nutrition should be fully supplied, and colds should be prevented.

Implementation of Pulmonary Disease Prevention 241

— Ding Huikang

The earlier a disease is discovered, the greater the hope of curing it. Everyone knows this. There is a saying that the best doctor treats the disease before it occurs. Therefore, the highest peak of medicine in our ideal belongs to the work of preventing diseases. It is too late to apply treatment after the disease occurs.

However, in clinical experiments, there are many diseases that have very little pain at the beginning. You must wait until the disease increases before you feel pain and seek medical treatment, such as heart, kidney, cancer, and syphilis. Pulmonary disease (pulmonary tuberculosis) is especially the case. In my annual observation of patients with pulmonary disease who come to the hospital for treatment, most of them have lost [the opportunity for proper treatment], so they are urgently seeking treatment when the disease is escalating. Most of the physical strength of this type of patient is too weak, so the treatment is extremely difficult. If they can be treated at the beginning, it will be twice the result with half the effort. The superiority of the treatment results can be asserted. However, given the immaturity of knowledge of our people and the lack of common knowledge about diseases, wanting them to be able to get early treatment is tantamount to blaming the blind to see things as equally impossible. Therefore, we can only rely on the efforts of our doctors to conduct examinations when patients think they are healthy in order to achieve the goal of early treatment, which is also the implementation of pulmonary disease prevention.

Pulmonary disease is an infectious disease. If it can be treated early, it can be easily eradicated. It is closely related to public health and social health. However, early examination is very difficult. If only percussion and auscultation are performed, it is really not enough to fully diagnose early pulmonary disease. The most reliable method of early diagnosis is to use X-rays for detailed examination to be able to see the crux of the problem.

Results of X-Ray Examination of People Who Consider Themselves Healthy 242

When we perform X-ray examinations on people who consider themselves healthy, we can often see calcified lesions and pleural adhesions, lung scars, etc. in their lungs. This kind is all non-progressive diseases, accounting for about 6% to 10% of the patients, especially those over 60 years old. However, patients with this kind of non-progressive pulmonary disease, although temporarily cured, often have the risk of recurrence and becoming progressive pulmonary disease.

Secondly, all progressive pulmonary diseases from initial infiltration to extremely severe open diseases can be detected. Most of them are from 15 to 60 or 70 years old. According to the statistics of Dr. Brawing, about 5 to 10 per thousand of the patients suffering from this kind of progressive pulmonary disease are initially considered to have absolutely healthy lungs.

Most people who are healthy in appearance but have pulmonary disease or open pulmonary disease do not know it, because their symptoms are very slight, so it is not easy to attract their attention. However, we must pay attention to these patients with unconscious pulmonary disease, because if they can be discovered early, on the one hand, it can be treated early, and on the other hand, it can be prevented from infection. 、

I once saw Mr. Gu Zheng, a physical educator, who was extremely strong. At first, he did not know that there was any pathological change in his lungs, but during the January 28 Incident, Mr. Gu became ill due to overwork in serving the Security Corps. In addition, a physical education instructor at Guanghua University, a native of Wuxi, also had a physique that was stronger than ordinary people, and had hemoptysis due to strenuous exercise. These lesions can be detected on X-rays. Therefore, if we can carry out strict X-ray examinations on people who usually consider themselves healthy, that is, for unconscious pulmonary disease, the more pulmonary diseases are discovered, the less hidden they will be. In other words, even if the patient has not noticed it himself, his lesions have been seen by us, which is of great importance to both treatment and prevention. This is the excellent result of performing X-ray examinations, and it is also the preliminary step in the implementation of pulmonary disease prevention.

In short, the unconscious period of pulmonary disease lasts for a long time. The necessary method of pulmonary disease prevention in our ideal is to conduct a general X-ray examination for all the people once or twice a year, so that the lesions can be detected and eradicated early when the patient has no pain. However, this move is extremely difficult to implement in practice. It is also not easy to find ways to conduct separate examinations in various groups such as schools, institutions, factories, and troops under the current situation of our country’s health administration. Even if the goal of this general examination can be achieved, it is only a small part of the entire healthy population. In other words, this kind of general X-ray examination, although extremely important, can only detect a part of the patients with unconscious pulmonary disease, and most of the patients with pulmonary disease will be discovered when they seek medical treatment.

Results of X-Ray Examination of Patients 243

Recently, Hormann’s statistics after examining various patients with X-rays are as follows.

Diagnosis: Pulmonary disease, pneumonia. Number of people: 884. After X-ray examination, 295 people were considered to have pulmonary tuberculosis, and 137 of them were open.

Diagnosis: Dry pleurisy. Number of people: 113. After X-ray examination, 16 people were considered to have pulmonary tuberculosis, and 5 of them were open. Diagnosis: Asthma, bronchitis, emphysema. Number of people: 165. After X-ray examination, 15 people were considered to have pulmonary tuberculosis, and 5 of them were open.

Diagnosis: Influenza, number of people examined within three weeks during the epidemic. Number of people: 163. After X-ray examination, 14 people were considered to have pulmonary tuberculosis, and 5 of them were open. Diagnosis: Influenza, number of people examined within three weeks when not epidemic. Number of people: 73. After X-ray examination, 14 people were considered to have pulmonary tuberculosis, and 6 of them were open. From this, it can be seen that there are many latent pulmonary diseases (pulmonary tuberculosis), and at the same time, there are open pulmonary diseases among them. Therefore, early diagnosis and timely treatment are as important as early detection of unconscious pulmonary diseases in preventing transmission, and should not be neglected by us. But when the patient first seeks medical treatment, the conscious symptoms are very slight and difficult to distinguish. Even if the patient has a considerable degree of illness, percussion and auscultation are also unreliable. It is really difficult to get an accurate diagnosis without X-ray examination. However, most doctors may not have X-ray equipment, so it is inevitable that they will be delayed. This is not only the case in our country, but also in developed countries in Europe and the United States.

Because pulmonary disease at the beginning mostly has very slight symptoms, or even no pain, and its symptoms are often similar to other diseases, it is easy to be misidentified.

However, for the sake of implementing prevention, if we cannot detect and eradicate these unconscious and latent pulmonary diseases as early as possible, how can we curb the spread of pulmonary disease? Therefore, preventing pulmonary disease is most effective by early diagnosis and treatment before the disease occurs, and for early diagnosis, there is really no other more reliable method than X-ray examination.
